**Failure mode**: When set to `unstructured`, partitioning errors are raised loudly — no silent fallback to legacy. This prevents hidden regressions.

### Adapter: Element → Block Mapping

`cookimport/parsing/unstructured_adapter.py` — single entry point:

```python
partition_html_to_blocks(
    html: str,
    *,
    spine_index: int,
    source_location_id: str,
) -> tuple[list[Block], list[dict]]
```

**Category mapping**:
- `Title` → `BlockType.TEXT`, `font_weight="bold"`, `is_heading=True`, `heading_level=clamp(depth+1, 1, 6)`
- `NarrativeText` / `UncategorizedText` → `BlockType.TEXT`
- `ListItem` → `BlockType.TEXT`, `is_list_item=True`
- `Table` → `BlockType.TABLE`
- Everything else → `BlockType.TEXT`

**Traceability features** stored on every Block:
- `spine_index` — absolute position in EPUB spine (for split-job merge ordering)
- `unstructured_element_id` — Unstructured's hash-based ID (may vary across versions)
- `unstructured_element_index` — sequential index within the spine document (stable)
- `unstructured_stable_key` — `"{source_location_id}:spine{spine_index}:e{element_index}"` (diff-friendly)
- `unstructured_category` — raw category string from Unstructured
- `unstructured_category_depth` — hierarchy depth (drives heading level)
- `unstructured_parent_id` — Unstructured parent element linkage
- `source_location_id` — book identifier for provenance correlation

**Text normalization**: Uses the same `cleaning.normalize_text()` pipeline as legacy (NFKC + whitespace standardization + mojibake repair). Applied in the adapter to avoid double-normalization.

**Ordering invariants**:
- Element order within each spine doc matches Unstructured's output order
- Spine docs iterated in ascending `spine_index`
- No sorting by text or category — ordering is the coordinate system for segmentation

### Block Roles

`cookimport/parsing/block_roles.py` — called after signal enrichment, for both extractors:

```python
assign_block_roles(blocks: list[Block]) -> None  # in-place
```

Deterministic, cheap heuristics. Stored as `Block.features["block_role"]`:

| Role | When assigned |
|---|---|
| `recipe_title` | Heading (h3+) with short text (≤80 chars) |
| `section_heading` | Heading (h1/h2) with short text |
| `ingredient_line` | `is_ingredient_likely`, `starts_with_quantity`, or ingredient header |
| `instruction_line` | `is_instruction_likely` or instruction header |
| `metadata` | `is_yield` or `is_time` |
| `tip_like` | Starts with "Note:", "Tip:", "Chef's note:", etc. |
| `narrative` | Substantive prose (≥15 words) |
| `other` | Everything else (short fragments, noise) |

**Block role counts are aggregated per chunk** during chunking (`chunks.py`) and stored in `provenance["block_role_counts"]`. The chunk lane scorer (`_score_lane`) uses these counts to adjust knowledge/noise scoring: recipe-structural roles (ingredient_line, instruction_line, recipe_title, metadata) boost the knowledge score proportionally, tip_like provides a small knowledge boost, and `other` roles add a slight noise bias.

### Diagnostics Artifact

When using the `unstructured` extractor, a `unstructured_elements.jsonl` raw artifact is emitted per run. Each line is a JSON object with:

```json
{
  "source_location_id": "book-name",
  "spine_index": 3,
  "element_index": 7,
  "element_id": "abc123...",
  "stable_key": "book-name:spine3:e7",
  "category": "Title",
  "category_depth": 1,
  "parent_id": "def456...",
  "text": "Chapter 2: Soups",
  "html_tag": null
}
```

The artifact metadata includes `unstructured_version` and `element_count`.

Located at: `raw/epub/<source_hash>/unstructured_elements.jsonl`

For split jobs (`--workers > 1`), each worker writes diagnostics under `.job_parts/`, merged to `raw/` on success.

### Split-Job Behavior

Unchanged from legacy. Each worker processes `[start_spine, end_spine)`:
- Blocks carry absolute `spine_index` for deterministic merge
- Diagnostics accumulate per-worker and merge with the block artifacts
- Known limitation preserved: recipes spanning spine boundaries can still be split

## Files

| File | Role |
|---|---|
| `cookimport/parsing/unstructured_adapter.py` | Element → Block mapping + diagnostics generation |
| `cookimport/parsing/block_roles.py` | Deterministic block_role assignment |
| `cookimport/plugins/epub.py` | Extractor switch, wired into ebooklib + ZIP paths |
| `cookimport/cli.py` | `--epub-extractor` CLI option + interactive Settings menu |
| `tests/test_unstructured_adapter.py` | 26 tests: adapter (14), split-merge (2), block_roles (10) |

## Key Decisions

| Decision | Rationale |
|---|---|
| Partition per spine doc (not `partition_epub`) | Preserves start_spine/end_spine splitting; avoids Pandoc/system deps |
| Store element_id + stable_key on every Block | Traceability for regression diffing |
| EPUB-only scope (no PDF) | PDF uses different upstream primitives (layout/OCR); separate adapter needed |
| Text normalization in adapter via `cleaning.normalize_text()` | One source of truth; avoids double-normalization |
| Hard-fail on Unstructured errors (no silent fallback) | Silent fallback hides regressions |
| block_roles run for both extractors | Cheap deterministic heuristics; benefits all paths |
| Pin `unstructured>=0.18.32,<0.19` | Avoid behavior drift; tested and stable |
| Default to `unstructured` extractor | Better semantic extraction; legacy available as fallback |

## Telemetry

Unstructured telemetry is suppressed at module import time:
- `DO_NOT_TRACK=true`
- `SCARF_NO_ANALYTICS=true`

Set in `unstructured_adapter.py` via `os.environ.setdefault()`.

## Quirks & Notes

- Unstructured 0.18.32 classifies short paragraphs as `UncategorizedText` and longer ones as `NarrativeText`. Both map to `BlockType.TEXT`; `block_role` handles the semantic distinction.
- `category_depth` on Title elements reflects HTML heading hierarchy: h1→0, h2→1, etc. This drives `heading_level = clamp(depth+1, 1, 6)`.
- The HTML partitioner doesn't require NLTK/punkt downloads (unlike PDF partitioning).

## Future

- PDF extraction via Unstructured is a separate follow-up plan — different upstream primitives (page/bbox/OCR lines) require a separate adapter and validation strategy.
- Optional: compare Unstructured `chunk_by_title` boundaries vs current chunker on non-recipe streams.
```

## docs/plans/I4.1-Auto-tag.md

```markdown
---
summary: "ExecPlan and implementation notes for catalog-driven recipe auto-tagging."
read_when:
  - When modifying tagging rules, policies, or CLI command behavior
  - When evaluating deterministic vs optional LLM tagging phases
---

# Auto-tag recipes with a catalog-driven rule engine (LLM-ready)

## What It Does

The tagging subsystem (`cookimport/tagging/`) automatically suggests recipe tags from the existing tag catalog. You point it at staged draft files or DB recipe rows and it returns a list of tags with confidence scores and human-readable evidence explaining each choice.

    # Suggest tags for staged drafts (dry run)
    cookimport tag-recipes suggest --draft-dir "data/output/<run>/final drafts/<workbook>/" \
      --catalog-json data/tagging/tag_catalog.json --explain

    # Apply tags to a DB recipe
    cookimport tag-recipes apply --db-url "$COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL" --recipe-id "<uuid>" \
      --catalog-json data/tagging/tag_catalog.json --apply

    # Export catalog from DB to JSON snapshot
    cookimport tag-catalog export --db-url "$COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL" --out data/tagging/tag_catalog.json

    # Inspect what the tagger "sees" for a given recipe
    cookimport tag-recipes debug-signals --draft path/to/r0.json

Example output:

    Recipe: Instant Pot Chicken Chili
    Suggested tags:
      - cooking-style/instant-pot (0.80)  matched 'instant pot' in title
      - main-protein/chicken (0.70)       matched chicken cut in ingredients
      - cooking-method/pressure-cook (0.60) matched pressure cook in instructions
      - dish-type/stew (0.70)             matched stew in title


## Design Principles

**Precision over recall.** Missing a tag is better than adding a wrong one, because DB writes are insert-only and there's no "who assigned this" tracking, so a bad tag can't be safely auto-removed later.

**Catalog-driven, not hard-coded.** Rules are keyed by tag `key_norm` (e.g., `instant-pot`), never by UUID. The engine skips any rule whose key doesn't exist in the loaded catalog, so adding new tags to the catalog requires zero code changes — the new tags simply become available.

**Deterministic first, LLM optional.** The deterministic engine runs on every recipe. The LLM second pass is gated behind `--llm`, disabled by default, and only invoked for categories the deterministic engine left empty. If no provider is configured, it warns once and continues with deterministic results.

**Insert-only DB writes.** All writes use `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (recipe_id, tag_id) DO NOTHING`. Re-running is safe. The system never deletes or replaces existing assignments.


## Architecture

The pipeline has four stages, each in its own module:

### 1. Catalog loading (`catalog.py`)

Three frozen dataclasses — `TagCategory`, `Tag`, `TagCatalog` — with lookup dicts (`tags_by_key`, `categories_by_id`, `tags_by_category_id`, etc.). The catalog can be loaded from Postgres (`load_catalog_from_db`) or from a JSON snapshot (`load_catalog_from_json`).

The JSON export includes a `catalog_fingerprint` (SHA-256 over a deterministic payload of all categories + tags). This fingerprint is recorded in every run report and checked before DB apply to catch catalog drift — if a tag ID in the snapshot no longer exists in the target DB, the apply aborts with a clear message.

DB queries assume `public.recipe_tag_categories` for categories and `public.recipe_tags` for tags. The category table name was inferred from conventions (the schema files were not in the repo at build time) and should be verified on first DB run.

### 2. Signal extraction (`signals.py`, `db_read.py`)

A `RecipeSignalPack` is a flat dataclass containing everything the engine needs to score a recipe:

- **Text fields:** title, description, notes (strings)
- **List fields:** ingredients, instructions (lists of strings)
- **Numeric fields:** prep/cook/total time in minutes, max oven temp in F, spice level, attention level, cleanup level, yield phrase

Two extractors build this pack:

- `signals_from_draft_json(path)` — reads a cookbook3 `RecipeDraftV1` JSON file, pulling `raw_text` from ingredient lines and `instruction` from steps, converting `cook_time_seconds` to minutes.
- `fetch_recipe_bundle(db_url, recipe_id)` — queries `public.recipes`, `public.recipe_steps`, and `public.step_ingredient_lines`.

Text normalization (`normalize_text_for_matching`) lowercases, strips Unicode accents (NFKD decomposition), replaces punctuation with spaces, and collapses whitespace. This means "Sautéed" becomes "sauteed" and "Café" becomes "cafe" for matching purposes.

### 3. Deterministic scoring (`rules.py`, `policies.py`, `engine.py`)

**Rules** (`rules.py`): A `TAG_RULES` dictionary with ~80 entries, each keyed by tag `key_norm`. Each rule has:

- `patterns`: list of `{field, regex, weight, evidence}` — the engine sums weights of all matched patterns to get a raw score (clamped to 0..1).
- `exclude_patterns` (optional): if any match, the tag is suppressed entirely.
- `min_score`: per-tag threshold (default 0.6).

Current rule coverage by category:

| Category | Tags covered | Signal source |
|----------|-------------|---------------|
| cooking-style | instant-pot, slow-cooker, air-fryer, grill, sheet-pan, one-pot, no-cook, stovetop-only, oven-only | Title + instructions |
| equipment | blender, immersion-blender, food-processor, dutch-oven, wok, cast-iron, stand-mixer, smoker | Instructions + title |
| cooking-method | bake, roast, steam, simmer, saute, braise, pressure-cook, deep-fry, fry, smoke, sous-vide, broil, poach | Instructions + title |
| effort | quick, hands-off-friendly, minimal-prep, beginner-friendly, weekend | Title + numeric (total_time, attention_level) |
| main-protein | chicken, beef, pork, fish, shrimp, tofu, chickpeas, lentils, eggs, lamb, turkey, beans, tempeh, seitan | **Ingredients** (primary), title (secondary) |
| main-carb | rice, pasta-noodles, potatoes, sweet-potatoes, tortillas, bread, quinoa, couscous | **Ingredients** (primary), title (secondary) |
| storage | freezer-friendly, meal-prep-friendly, make-ahead, batch-cooking | Notes + description + title |
| meal-type | breakfast, dessert, snack | Title + description |
| course | appetizer, side-dish, sauce, drink, condiment, dressing | Title |
| dish-type | soup, stew, salad, sandwich, pasta, curry, casserole, stir-fry, tacos, pizza, bowl, rice-dish, wrap, baked-goods | Title |
| cuisine, dietary, flavor-profile, heat-source, vibe, season, holiday, techniques | *No deterministic rules yet* | Reserved for LLM second pass |

Rule authoring lessons learned:

- **Protein/carb rules should be ingredient-driven.** Title-only matches cause false positives (e.g., "Chicken Stock" is not a chicken recipe). The current approach uses high-weight patterns for specific cuts ("chicken breast", "beef chuck") and low-weight fallback for generic mentions ("chicken", "beef").
- **Don't use exclude patterns for broth/stock.** An exclude pattern on "beef broth" suppresses the entire tag even when "beef chuck" also appears in the same recipe's ingredients. Instead, the separate-pattern-weight approach naturally handles this: a recipe with only "beef broth" scores low (0.3) and misses the threshold, while "beef chuck" + "beef broth" scores high (1.0).
- **Cooking method weights must be >= 0.6.** Methods like "simmer" and "sauté" typically appear only in instructions (never titles), so a single instruction-field match needs to clear the threshold on its own.

**Policies** (`policies.py`): A `CATEGORY_POLICIES` dictionary defines constraints per category:

- `mode: "single"` — only the highest-confidence tag is kept (main-protein, main-carb, meal-type, course, dish-type).
- `mode: "multi"` — all tags above threshold, up to `max_tags` (equipment, cooking-method, effort, storage, occasion).
- `min_confidence: 0.6` — default threshold (can be overridden per-tag via `min_score` in the rule).

**Engine** (`engine.py`): `suggest_tags_deterministic(catalog, signals)` runs all rules against the signal pack:

1. Lazily compiles all regex patterns once (module-level cache).
2. Normalizes text fields on first access (per-call cache).
3. For each tag rule: checks excludes, sums matched pattern weights, applies threshold.
4. Adds numeric-based suggestions (quick from total_time, hands-off from attention_level).
5. Groups by category and applies single/multi policies.
6. Returns sorted `list[TagSuggestion]`, each with `tag_key`, `category_key`, `confidence`, and `evidence`.

### 4. LLM second pass (`llm_second_pass.py`) — scaffolded, not wired

The `--llm` flag on `suggest` and `apply` enables a gated second pass that only runs for categories the deterministic engine left empty. The flow:

1. Identify missing categories (categories with policies defined but no deterministic suggestions).
2. For each, build a candidate shortlist (up to 10 tags) via token overlap between tag display names and the recipe's combined text.
3. Call the LLM with candidates + recipe context, expecting a structured JSON response.
4. Validate strictly: tag must exist in catalog, must match stated category, must be in candidate shortlist, confidence 0..1.
5. Merge with deterministic results and re-apply category policies.

Currently uses a mock provider that returns an empty list. If no provider is configured, warns once and falls back to deterministic-only.


## Module Layout

    cookimport/tagging/
    ├── __init__.py
    ├── catalog.py          Tag/Category models, DB + JSON loaders, fingerprinting
    ├── signals.py          RecipeSignalPack, text normalization, draft extraction
    ├── db_read.py          RecipeSignalPack extraction from Postgres
    ├── rules.py            TAG_RULES dictionary (~80 regex rules)
    ├── policies.py         CATEGORY_POLICIES (single/multi, thresholds, max_tags)
    ├── engine.py           Scoring engine, numeric rules, policy enforcement
    ├── render.py           Console text + JSON output formatting + run reports
    ├── db_write.py         Idempotent INSERT for recipe_tag_assignments
    ├── llm_second_pass.py  LLM scaffolding (disabled by default)
    ├── eval.py             Precision/recall evaluation harness
    ├── cli.py              Typer commands wired into main app
    └── README.md

    tests/
    ├── test_tagging.py            19 unit + regression tests
    └── tagging_gold/
        ├── tag_catalog.small.json   8-category, 30-tag fixture catalog
        ├── fixtures.json            8 fixture recipes
        └── gold_labels.json         Expected tags per fixture


## CLI Reference

**`cookimport tag-catalog export`** — Export the tag catalog from Postgres to a JSON snapshot.

| Flag | Default | Notes |
|------|---------|-------|
| `--db-url` | `$COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL` | Postgres connection string |
| `--out` | required | Output path for `tag_catalog.json` |

**`cookimport tag-recipes suggest`** — Suggest tags for draft files (does not write to DB).

| Flag | Default | Notes |
|------|---------|-------|
| `--draft` | | Single draft JSON path |
| `--draft-dir` | | Folder of drafts (recursive `*.json`) |
| `--catalog-json` | required | Path to exported catalog |
| `--out-dir` | | Write `*.tags.json` per recipe |
| `--explain` | false | Show evidence strings |
| `--limit N` | all | Process at most N recipes |
| `--llm` | false | Enable LLM second pass |

Always writes a `tagging_report.json` with aggregate stats (per-category counts, zero-tag recipes, catalog fingerprint).

**`cookimport tag-recipes apply`** — Tag recipes in the database (dry-run by default).

| Flag | Default | Notes |
|------|---------|-------|
| `--db-url` | `$COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL` | Postgres connection string |
| `--recipe-id` | | Single recipe UUID |
| `--import-batch-id` | | Scope to batch (for bulk) |
| `--source` | | Scope to source string |
| `--limit` | 100 | Max recipes in batch |
| `--catalog-json` | required | Path to exported catalog |
| `--apply` | false | Actually write (default is dry-run) |
| `--yes` | false | Skip confirmation prompt |
| `--explain` | false | Show evidence |
| `--min-confidence` | | Override minimum confidence threshold |
| `--llm` | false | Enable LLM second pass |

Before writing, verifies every selected tag ID still exists in the target DB. Aborts on drift.

**`cookimport tag-recipes debug-signals`** — Print the signal pack the tagger sees for a recipe.

| Flag | Notes |
|------|-------|
| `--draft` | Path to draft JSON |
| `--db-url` + `--recipe-id` | Fetch from Postgres |


## Testing

19 tests in `tests/test_tagging.py`, all deterministic, running in ~0.06s:

- **Catalog:** load/roundtrip, lookup helpers.
- **Signals:** text normalization, dict-to-signal conversion.
- **Engine scoring:** per-fixture assertions (instant pot chicken, slow cooker beef stew, grilled salmon, quick pasta, sheet pan chicken, tofu stir fry, no-cook salad, dutch oven pot roast).
- **Policy enforcement:** single-category picks at most one tag.
- **Edge cases:** tags missing from catalog are skipped, evidence is always present, deterministic outputs are identical across runs.
- **Gold set regression:** 8 fixture recipes with labeled expected tags. Asserts overall precision >= 70%, single-category precision >= 80%, overall recall >= 50%.

To run: `pytest tests/test_tagging.py -v`


## How to Extend

**Add a new deterministic rule:** Edit `rules.py`, add an entry to `TAG_RULES` keyed by the tag's `key_norm`:

    "my-new-tag": {
        "min_score": 0.6,
        "patterns": [
            {"field": "ingredients", "regex": r"\bmy pattern\b", "weight": 0.7,
             "evidence": "matched X in ingredients"},
        ],
    }

Then add a fixture recipe + gold label in `tests/tagging_gold/` and a test case in `test_tagging.py`. Run the gold set regression test to verify you haven't broken precision.

**Add a new tag to the catalog (no code change needed):** Add the tag to the DB seed, re-export the catalog JSON. If no rule exists for the new `key_norm`, it simply won't get deterministic suggestions (but will be available to the LLM second pass when wired).

**Wire a real LLM provider:** Implement `_check_provider_configured()` and replace `_mock_llm_call()` in `llm_second_pass.py`. The validation logic (`_validate_llm_response`) is already implemented and enforces: tag exists in catalog, category matches, confidence 0..1, tag is in candidate shortlist.


## Key Decisions

- **Rules keyed by `key_norm`, not UUID** — forward-compatible with catalog changes. Rules for tags that don't exist in the loaded catalog are silently skipped.
- **Separate tagging CLI module** — `cookimport/tagging/cli.py` wired via `app.add_typer()` to keep the 2700-line main `cli.py` manageable.
- **`psycopg[binary]` as optional dependency** — added to `[db]` and `[dev]` extras in `pyproject.toml`. File-based tagging works without it.
- **Category table assumed `public.recipe_tag_categories`** — inferred from conventions; `db/schema.snapshot.sql` and `supabase/seeds/catalog.sql` were not in the repo. Verify on first DB run.
- **Protein patterns use weight tiers, not excludes** — a high-weight pattern for specific cuts ("beef chuck" = 0.7) and a low-weight fallback for generic mentions ("beef" = 0.3). This avoids the "beef broth excludes beef chuck" problem that exclude patterns caused.


## Known Gaps

- **Gold set is small** (8 recipes). Target 50 for meaningful regression protection.
- **No deterministic rules** for cuisine, dietary, flavor-profile, heat-source, vibe, season, holiday, or techniques. These are reserved for the LLM pass.
- **LLM provider not wired** — scaffolding exists but uses a mock that returns empty.
- **Category table name unverified** against production DB.
- **No DB integration tests** — DB code is covered by unit tests + manual acceptance.
```

## docs/plans/I5.1-golden-set-freeform.md

```markdown
---
summary: "ExecPlan for freeform-span golden-set workflows and evaluation contracts."
read_when:
  - When running or revising freeform Label Studio annotation campaigns
  - When aligning freeform export/eval artifacts with benchmark workflows
---

# ExecPlan: Option A — Freeform Spans Golden Set for Recipe Structure (+ Yield/Time), No Tag Annotation

This ExecPlan is a living document. Keep **Progress**, **Surprises & Discoveries**, **Decision Log**, and **Outcomes & Retrospective** up to date as you execute. Maintain this plan in accordance with `docs/PLANS.md`.

## Purpose / Intent (why this matters)

We need a ground-truth dataset to measure whether cookbook ingestion correctly turns messy sources into structured recipes. The highest-leverage human signal is **structure** (titles, ingredient lines, instruction lines, and non-recipe text), because that directly drives downstream parsing, linking, and recipe creation.

Option A deliberately minimizes annotation burden: a small, stable span label set for structure, plus two practical metadata lines (**yield/servings** and **time**) that strongly affect schema alignment. We explicitly avoid asking annotators to label against a large, evolving tag taxonomy (throughput + consistency killer).

Observable “it worked” outcome:

- Label Studio shows a **freeform-spans** project where annotators highlight spans with labels including `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE`.
- `cookimport labelstudio-export --export-scope freeform-spans` produces:
  - `freeform_span_labels.jsonl`
  - `freeform_segment_manifest.jsonl`
  - `summary.json` (and the raw `labelstudio_export.json`)
- `cookimport labelstudio-eval freeform-spans` produces:
  - `eval_report.md`
  - `eval_report.json`
  - `missed_gold_spans.jsonl`
  - `false_positive_preds.jsonl`

## Glossary (terms used here)

- **Source file**: the exact input file bytes (EPUB/PDF/etc.). If bytes change, the source identity changes and eval can collapse to near-zero.
- **Block**: an ordered unit of extracted text with a `block_index` (EPUB paragraph/list item, PDF line/OCR line, etc.).
- **Segment**: a contiguous window of blocks used for freeform annotation, with deterministic ID:
  - `urn:cookimport:segment:{source_hash}:{start_block_index}:{end_block_index}`
- **Gold**: spans labeled by humans in freeform-spans projects, exported as `freeform_span_labels.jsonl`.
- **Predictions (“pred-run”)**: for freeform eval, this is typically the **pipeline** task-scope import run folder (it contains `label_studio_tasks.jsonl` that eval maps into predicted ranges).
- **Write consent**: `--allow-labelstudio-write`. Non-interactive import/benchmark require it; treat as “yes, I intend to upload tasks.”

## Scope (and non-goals)

In scope:

- Freeform spans golden set for structure labels, plus additive `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE`.
- Preserve offset stability (no whitespace normalization changes in freeform rendering).
- Export + eval accept and report new labels without breaking legacy “strict” headline metrics.
- Pilot (3–5 books) → v1 (10–20 books), plus a labeling guide and basic QA/IAA.

Non-goals:

- Manual tagging against the large tag catalog.
- PDF image box annotation workflows (not the current integration).
- Re-architecting benchmark; only guardrails and clarity improvements needed to run safely.

## Progress

- [ ] (2026-02-12) Confirm “Option A” scope + success metrics with stakeholders: freeform spans for structure, plus yield/time lines; **no manual tagging against the 203-tag catalog**.
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Pick a pilot corpus (3–5 cookbooks) that spans: clean EPUB, messy EPUB, and at least one PDF (scanned vs non-scanned if available).
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Run baseline workflow end-to-end on 1 pilot book:
  - freeform import → annotate a few segments → export gold
  - pipeline import (pred-run)
  - freeform eval
  Verify environment, paths, and report artifacts.
- [x] (2026-02-12) Update freeform Label Studio config to add `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE` (keeping existing labels intact); keep whitespace-preserving rendering unchanged.
- [x] (2026-02-12) Update export + eval handling so new labels are accepted and reported without breaking legacy exports or existing "strict" headline metrics.
- [ ] (2026-02-14) Write a 1-page labeling guide (with examples) and add it to the repo docs; include “what not to label” rules (e.g., tags, narrative fluff).
- [ ] (2026-02-15) Import pilot tasks with consistent segmentation settings.
- [ ] (2026-02-16) Complete pilot annotations (single annotator) and export gold.
- [ ] (2026-02-17) Run eval; review errors + diagnostics; refine guide + definitions if needed.
- [ ] (2026-02-18) Add second annotator pass for a subset (10–20% of segments) to estimate inter-annotator agreement.
- [ ] (2026-02-20) Expand from pilot to v1 dataset (10–20 cookbooks), cut a release artifact folder, and (optionally) document how this ties into benchmark usage.

## Surprises & Discoveries (keep updated)

- Freeform workflows are segment-based and rely on deterministic IDs for resume/idempotence. This is powerful, but it can surprise you when you want to "re-import the same book" (IAA, reannotation) unless you isolate output dirs.
- Freeform labels intentionally preserve whitespace in the UI to keep offsets stable; any "cleanup" normalization risks breaking span offsets.
- Non-interactive commands default under a golden-root folder and uploads are gated by explicit write-consent flags; accidental upload risk is real if people muscle-memory CLI commands.
- The existing catalog contains a large set of recipe tags; asking annotators to label against that set is a throughput killer and adds consistency risk.
- (2026-02-12) The pipeline does not yet produce dedicated yield/time chunk types — yield/time lines are currently classified as headers or OTHER by the general classifier. The `_map_chunk_to_label` mappings for YIELD_LINE/TIME_LINE are future-proofed but will only activate when the pipeline adds those chunk types. Freeform gold annotations will still capture yield/time from human labeling.
- (2026-02-12) The export path (`export.py`) is label-agnostic for freeform spans — it passes through whatever labels annotators apply. No export changes were needed for new labels.
- (2026-02-12) Added backward-compat aliases `YIELD` → `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME` → `TIME_LINE` in label normalization, following the same pattern as `KNOWLEDGE` → `TIP`.

## Decision Log

- **2026-02-12 — Choose Option A (Minimal Human Labeling):** Build a freeform spans golden set focused on structural recipe extraction (title/ingredient/instruction/etc.) and *optionally* yield/time lines; do **not** require humans to label a large tag taxonomy.
- **2026-02-12 — Keep Freeform “Strict Metrics” Stable:** Add yield/time labels as additive diagnostics so headline metrics remain comparable across time; don’t silently redefine the main benchmark.
- **2026-02-12 — Segmentation Defaults:** Start with segment size ~40 blocks and overlap ~5 blocks; adjust only if pilot shows systematic boundary misses.
- **2026-02-12 — Keep freeform gold separate from pipeline preds:** Freeform eval compares gold spans to predictions mapped from pipeline chunks, so treat the “pred-run” as a pipeline import run folder (not the freeform run folder).

## Plan of Work

### Phase 0 — Align on “What we’re measuring”

This is a **structure-first** golden set. Annotators label only spans that correspond to recipe structure (and optionally yield/time lines). Everything else becomes `OTHER`. The dataset is designed to support repeatable benchmarking and to localize failures (ingredients vs narrative, instruction boundary drift, yield/time missed, etc.).

### Phase 1 — Taxonomy + Label Studio config changes (small + additive)

Add two new labels to the existing freeform label config:

- `YIELD_LINE` — spans expressing yield/servings (e.g., “Serves 4”, “Makes 2 loaves”).
- `TIME_LINE` — spans expressing prep/cook/total time (e.g., “Prep: 10 min”, “Total time 1 hour”).

Hard constraints:

- No renaming/removal of existing labels.
- Keep offset stability (preserve whitespace / pre-wrap rendering).
- Do not alter legacy normalization mappings (if older exports exist).

Concrete code touch points to inspect and likely update:

- `cookimport/labelstudio/label_config_freeform.py` (labels + rendering)
- `cookimport/labelstudio/export.py` (freeform export shaping/validation, if any)
- `cookimport/labelstudio/eval_freeform.py` (label normalization + reporting)

Testing expectations:

- Update/add tests in:
  - `tests/test_labelstudio_freeform.py` (config includes new labels; export accepts them)
  - `tests/test_labelstudio_export.py` (fixture with new labels passes)
  - Any eval report/snapshot tests to ensure strict metrics do not change while diagnostics include yield/time counts.

### Phase 2 — Pilot dataset creation (3–5 books)

Goal: validate segmentation, labeling guidance, export/eval reproducibility, and the practical edge cases (messy EPUB + at least one PDF).

Pilot success criteria:

- Imports produce stable task artifacts and reasonable `coverage.json` (no large silent gaps).
- Annotators can label without constantly “what label is this?” questions.
- Exports are generated without patching.
- Eval produces reports and the failure cases are debuggable back to segments.

Segmentation defaults (freeze for pilot):

- `segment_blocks = 40`
- `segment_overlap = 5`

If pilot shows systematic boundary misses (e.g., yield lines often split), adjust once and version the dataset cut. Do not change segmentation mid-campaign without versioning; it changes segment IDs and complicates merges.

### Phase 3 — Evaluation integration (strict metrics stable + yield/time as diagnostics)

Key requirement: keep existing headline/strict metrics comparable over time. The safest pattern:

- Include `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE` in exports.
- In freeform eval reporting, treat yield/time as **additive diagnostics** (counts + per-label metrics), not part of the strict aggregate unless you explicitly version/change the headline metric definition.

### Phase 4 — Scale to v1 (10–20 books) + QA + IAA

Scale annotation with:

- A clear labeling guide.
- Periodic spot checks (20 segments/book).
- A 10–20% overlap subset labeled by a second annotator to estimate agreement and highlight ambiguity.

Produce a versioned dataset bundle folder with:

- corpus list (files + hashes),
- segmentation params,
- label set version,
- date range + annotators,
- known caveats (OCR-heavy PDFs, etc.),
- per-book eval reports.

## Risks and Mitigations (plus footguns)

### Offset drift / unstable spans
Mitigation: preserve whitespace in rendered text; prohibit normalization; add a smoke test that offsets still align to exported segment text.

### Accidental uploads / write-side effects
Mitigation: keep write-consent explicit; document “no write without intent”; keep pilot/v1 projects clearly named.

### Benchmark side effects + gold discovery footgun
Non-interactive benchmark always uploads predictions first; it is not “eval-only.” Also, gold discovery searches both `data/golden/**` and `data/output/**`. If multiple gold exports exist, it can select the wrong one.
Mitigation: run benchmark in a clean workspace (or use explicit paths via `labelstudio-eval`); avoid mixing unrelated exports in the same roots during a campaign.

### Source identity mismatches leading to “zero match” eval
Mitigation: keep the exact source bytes stable; avoid renames/cutdown variants during labeling. Do not default to `--force-source-match`; use it only when you knowingly compare variants and accept the risk of masking mismatches.

### Segmentation too small/large
Mitigation: tune after pilot; version if changed; do not change mid-run.

### Label ambiguity (NOTES vs TIP vs OTHER; yield/time boundaries)
Mitigation: crisp definitions + examples; add an “if unsure, label OTHER unless clearly TIP/NOTES” rule; adjudicate repeated disagreements.

## Definition of Done

- Freeform label config includes `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE` and preserves existing labels + offset-stable rendering.
- Exported gold includes:
  - `freeform_span_labels.jsonl`
  - `freeform_segment_manifest.jsonl`
  - `summary.json` (and raw export)
- Freeform eval runs cleanly on pilot and v1 datasets and produces:
  - `eval_report.json`
  - `eval_report.md`
  - `missed_gold_spans.jsonl`
  - `false_positive_preds.jsonl`
- A concise labeling guide exists with:
  - label definitions + boundary rules,
  - “what not to label” section,
  - yield/time edge cases,
  - versioned segmentation settings.
- v1 dataset bundle (10–20 books) is reproducible from documented commands and ready to be used as a benchmarking input.

## Labels (Freeform-Spans)

Base labels (existing):

- `RECIPE_TITLE`
- `INGREDIENT_LINE`
- `INSTRUCTION_LINE`
- `TIP`
- `NOTES`
- `VARIANT`
- `OTHER`

Additive labels (Option A extension):

- `YIELD_LINE`
- `TIME_LINE`

High-level labeling rules:

- Label the smallest span that cleanly expresses the target.
- Prefer line-level spans for ingredients/instructions/yield/time.
- If unsure whether something is “real recipe content” vs prose, label `OTHER` unless it clearly fits `TIP` or `NOTES`.

## Recommended CLI Runbook (Non-Interactive)

Prereqs:

- Label Studio running + env vars set:
  - `LABEL_STUDIO_URL`
  - `LABEL_STUDIO_API_KEY`

Notes on output roots:

- Label Studio CLI defaults its artifacts under `data/golden/` (not `data/output/`).
- Non-interactive upload/write is gated by `--allow-labelstudio-write`.

### 1) Import (freeform spans) — gold project

Use consistent segmentation settings for the entire campaign:

    cookimport labelstudio-import data/input/<book>.epub \
      --task-scope freeform-spans \
      --segment-blocks 40 \
      --segment-overlap 5 \
      --allow-labelstudio-write

Annotate in Label Studio.

### 2) Export gold

    cookimport labelstudio-export \
      --project-name "<Freeform Project Name>" \
      --export-scope freeform-spans

Record the resulting path to:

- `<gold_spans_jsonl>` = `.../exports/freeform_span_labels.jsonl`

### 3) Import (pipeline) — prediction run (“pred-run”)

Freeform eval expects predicted labeled ranges mapped from pipeline chunks, so generate a pipeline run folder:

    cookimport labelstudio-import data/input/<book>.epub \
      --task-scope pipeline \
      --chunk-level both \
      --allow-labelstudio-write

Record `<pred_run_dir>` = the run folder created for this pipeline import (it contains `label_studio_tasks.jsonl`).

### 4) Eval (freeform spans)

Default: do NOT force-match unless you explicitly accept comparing variants.

    cookimport labelstudio-eval freeform-spans \
      --pred-run <pred_run_dir> \
      --gold-spans <gold_spans_jsonl> \
      --output-dir data/golden/<ts>/eval-freeform/<book_slug>/

If (and only if) you intentionally compare renamed/cutdown variants, you may add `--force-source-match`, but document why.

### 5) Benchmark (convenience, but upload-first)

    cookimport labelstudio-benchmark \
      --allow-labelstudio-write

Warning: benchmark is upload-first; it will import/upload predictions before scoring. Also, gold discovery searches both `data/golden/**` and `data/output/**`; clean your workspace or use explicit `labelstudio-eval` paths for safety.

## Dataset Versioning

For every dataset cut, record:

- corpus list (books + versions/hashes),
- segmentation params (`segment_blocks`, `segment_overlap`),
- label set version (including yield/time enabled),
- date range + annotators,
- known caveats (OCR-heavy PDFs, etc.).

## Practical Quality Checks

- Randomly sample 20 segments per book:
  - confirm RECIPE_TITLE vs section headers are consistent,
  - confirm ingredients aren’t being confused with instruction steps,
  - confirm yield/time are consistently captured when present.
- After export, spot-check:
  - span offsets still align to displayed text,
  - touched block indices look plausible (no wildly out-of-range indices).

## Outcomes & Retrospective

(To be completed after v1 dataset ships.)

- What changed in extraction quality?
- Where did label ambiguity remain?
- What should be automated next?
```

## docs/plans/I6.1-integrate-LLM.md

```markdown
---
summary: "ExecPlan for integrating optional LLM repair into the import pipeline."
read_when:
  - When enabling or auditing LLM repair behavior in stage workflows
  - When updating LLM telemetry, gating, or fallback rules
---

# ExecPlan: I6 — Unmock + integrate LLM Repair into cookimport (ingredient parsing + step ↔ ingredient linking)

This ExecPlan is a living document. The sections **Progress**, **Surprises & Discoveries**, **Decision Log**, and **Outcomes & Retrospective** must be kept up to date as work proceeds.

This plan must be maintained in accordance with `docs/PLANS.md` at the repository root.

## Purpose / Big Picture

After this change, a user can optionally enable an “LLM Repair” layer when running the pipeline (for example via `cookimport stage ...`) to improve:

* structured ingredient parsing for tricky ingredient lines, and
* step ↔ ingredient linking for ingredients that the deterministic linker cannot confidently place.

The default behavior remains deterministic and unchanged: **LLM Repair is OFF unless explicitly enabled**.

A user can *see* the feature working by:

* running the same golden-set evaluation twice (LLM OFF vs LLM ON) and observing improved freeform/canonical eval artifacts (for example fewer missed ingredient-line spans), and
* opening the per-file conversion report and seeing an `llm` stats section (calls, cache hits, failures, repairs applied, time), and
* inspecting per-run JSONL artifacts that show exactly which lines were repaired, what the deterministic output was, what the LLM suggested, and whether it was applied.

## Progress

* [ ] (2026-02-12) Record baseline golden-set benchmark metrics with LLM OFF; archive the eval output folder path(s).
* [ ] (2026-02-12) Unmock `cookimport/llm/`: implement a real provider client, disk cache, and strict schema validation, with safe fallback behavior.
* [ ] (2026-02-12) Wire ingredient-line repair (gated + patch-based) into `cookimport/parsing/ingredients.py`, and write `ingredient_repairs.jsonl`.
* [ ] (2026-02-12) Extend per-file conversion report to include `llm` stats, and confirm it renders in existing perf/report flows.
* [ ] (2026-02-12) Re-run golden-set benchmark with ingredient repair ON; compare eval artifacts to baseline; capture a small “before vs after” summary in this plan.
* [ ] (2026-02-12) Wire step-link repair for unmatched/low-confidence cases into `cookimport/parsing/step_ingredients.py`, and write `step_link_repairs.jsonl`.
* [ ] (2026-02-12) Add unit tests for cache, schema validation, gating, and “repair only applies when allowed.”
* [ ] (2026-02-12) Re-run golden-set benchmark with ingredient + step-link repair ON; compare to baseline; tune thresholds/prompts with evidence.
* [ ] (2026-02-12) Document how to enable/disable LLM repair safely (flags + env vars), including a dry-run mode.

## Surprises & Discoveries

(Empty — fill as you learn things that change the plan. Keep entries dated and include small evidence snippets like test output or a linkable artifact path.)

## Decision Log

(Empty — record decisions that would be hard to reconstruct later, like threshold defaults, schema shapes, prompt versioning, cache key design, or why a repair rule was added/removed. Keep entries dated.)

## Outcomes & Retrospective

(Empty — after completion, summarize what moved metrics, what didn’t, and what you’d do next.)

## Context and Orientation

### What “cookimport” is (relevant subset)

`cookimport` is a Python 3.12 recipe ingestion + normalization pipeline:

* Importers ingest many formats into a common `ConversionResult`.
* Staging converts recipe candidates into final “cookbook3” drafts (internal model: `RecipeDraftV1`).
* During staging, it runs deterministic parsing steps including:

  * ingredient line parsing (`cookimport/parsing/ingredients.py`)
  * step ↔ ingredient linking (`cookimport/parsing/step_ingredients.py`)

The system is explicitly “deterministic-first”: ML/LLM features must not silently change the default pipeline outputs.

### Where outputs and reports go (important for validation)

A `cookimport stage ...` run writes outputs under:

* `data/output/<YYYY-MM-DD_HH.MM.SS>/...`

The per-file conversion report is written at the run root as:

* `data/output/<run_ts>/<workbook_slug>.excel_import_report.json`

Do not assume a `reports/` subfolder exists; many prior notes/docs drifted on this.

### Label Studio benchmark behavior (critical footgun)

The CLI benchmark command:

* `cookimport labelstudio-benchmark`

…is **upload-first** in non-interactive mode and will import/upload prediction tasks before evaluating, unless you’re using an interactive menu flow that supports eval-only. Non-interactive commands that write to Label Studio are gated by an explicit consent flag (see Concrete Steps).

### Current state of LLM support

There is already a directory `cookimport/llm/`, but it is currently **mocked** (calls return mock data). This plan replaces “mocked by default” with “real implementation available, but never used unless enabled.”

## Plan of Work

### Milestone 0 — Baseline: lock in “before” numbers

Goal: produce a baseline evaluation run (LLM OFF) that you can diff against later.

What exists at the end:

* a known run folder path (or benchmark eval folder path) containing:

  * `eval_report.json`
  * `eval_report.md`
  * `missed_gold_spans.jsonl`
  * `false_positive_preds.jsonl`

Work:

* Run your standard golden-set evaluation workflow exactly as you normally do today.
* Save the output directory path(s) in **Artifacts and Notes** in this plan (so future work can diff).

Acceptance:

* You can point to a concrete folder on disk that contains the eval artifacts above and is clearly labeled “baseline / LLM off”.

### Milestone 1 — Unmock `cookimport/llm/`: real provider + cache + strict validation

Goal: implement a safe, testable LLM client that only ever returns validated structured JSON, and that is fully cacheable and replayable.

What exists at the end:

* A real `cookimport/llm/` implementation that can:

  * perform a JSON-returning request to a provider (or be swapped for a fake provider in tests),
  * parse JSON strictly (no “best effort”),
  * validate against a Pydantic schema (project already uses Pydantic v2),
  * cache responses to disk with atomic writes, and
  * expose per-run stats counters (calls, hits, failures, seconds, repairs applied).

Design constraints (non-negotiable):

* If disabled, **must not**:

  * make network calls,
  * require an API key,
  * or change outputs.
* Any failure (timeout, invalid JSON, schema mismatch, rate limit) must degrade to a safe “no repair applied” behavior.

Implementation detail guidance:

* Prefer Pydantic models (or `TypeAdapter`) for validation, because the project is already Pydantic-heavy.
* Keep provider plumbing isolated (no provider-specific code in parsing modules).
* Add a `PROMPT_VERSION` constant that is included in the cache key so you can intentionally bust cache when prompt/schema changes.

Recommended interface (internal):

* In `cookimport/llm/client.py` (or similar), define something like:

  * `class LLMClient:`

    * `def complete_json(self, *, task_name: str, schema_id: str, prompt: str, cache_key: str, timeout_s: float | None = None) -> dict | None:`

Where:

* returning `None` means “no valid repair available” (caller must fall back).
* `schema_id` is a stable string like `ingredient_repair_v1` to help debugging.

Caching guidance:

* Cache key should include (at minimum):

  * task name
  * schema id
  * model id
  * prompt version
  * normalized prompt text

* Write cache files atomically (temp + rename).

* Concurrency footgun: atomic rename prevents partial files, but does not prevent two workers from both calling the provider on a cold cache. If this matters in your workload, add a simple per-key lock file (atomic create of `<key>.lock`), or accept the possibility of occasional duplicate calls in parallel runs.

### Milestone 2 — Ingredient-line repair (primary win)

Goal: keep deterministic parsing as the base, but add an opt-in “repair” pass for low-confidence/suspicious ingredient lines.

What exists at the end:

* When `--llm-repair=ingredients` is enabled (and global LLM enable is on), low-confidence ingredient lines will:

  * be sent to the LLM repair task,
  * validated strictly against a known schema,
  * sanity-checked against invariants,
  * applied only as a patch if safe,
  * and logged to `ingredient_repairs.jsonl`.

Where to integrate:

* `cookimport/parsing/ingredients.py` (the ingredient parsing entrypoint).
* If the actual staging pipeline calls a helper like `parse_ingredient_line(...)`, integrate there so all importers benefit.

Gating (default rules, tuned later with evidence):

* Call the LLM only if:

  * deterministic `confidence` is below a threshold (start at 0.75), or
  * deterministic output is structurally broken for a non-header line (for example empty ingredient text), or
  * a “looks like quantity” signal exists but the parse did not produce a plausible quantity kind.

Hard limits:

* Max repair calls per recipe (start: 6).
* Never call for obvious section headers (`quantity_kind == "section_header"`), unless you can justify and test a header-uncertainty detector.

Schema (ingredient repair v1):

The LLM must return a JSON object with these fields aligned to what the parser already emits:

* `quantity_kind`: `"exact" | "approximate" | "unquantified" | "section_header"`
* `input_qty`: number or null
* `raw_unit_text`: string or null
* `raw_ingredient_text`: string (required unless section_header)
* `preparation`: string or null
* `note`: string or null
* `is_optional`: boolean
* `confidence`: number 0..1 (recorded; never blindly trusted)
* `raw_text`: string (must exactly match the normalized input line you provided)

Validation / invariants (non-negotiable):

* If `quantity_kind == "exact"`, `input_qty` must be > 0.
* If `quantity_kind != "exact"`, `input_qty` must be null.
* `raw_text` must exactly match the input normalized line (reject if the LLM “edited” it).
* If the repaired result is invalid or violates invariants, do not apply; fall back to deterministic parse.

Patch application:

* Store (in-memory and/or artifacts) both:

  * deterministic parse (base),
  * candidate repair parse (if any),
  * final chosen parse.
* Mark repair metadata including cache key, model, latency, and reason applied/rejected.

Artifacts:

* Under the run folder, write:

  * `data/output/<run_ts>/rawArtifacts/llm/ingredient_repairs.jsonl`

Each JSONL line should include enough to debug without rerunning:

* recipe identifier (whatever stable ID exists in staging)
* ingredient line index
* input normalized line
* base parse (structured)
* llm output (structured or null)
* validation result and rejection reason if any
* final parse (structured)
* cache metadata (cache_key, hit/miss, latency_ms)

### Milestone 3 — Step ↔ ingredient linking repair (secondary, strict fallback)

Goal: do not replace the deterministic two-phase linker. Only use the LLM to rescue cases the linker already considered “no good answer.”

What exists at the end:

* With `--llm-repair=step_link` or `--llm-repair=all`, the linker will optionally attempt repair for:

  * ingredients that were not assigned to any step, and/or
  * extremely low-confidence assignments (only if the code has such a concept; don’t invent one without evidence).

Where to integrate:

* `cookimport/parsing/step_ingredients.py`
* Prefer to integrate at a point where you have:

  * the list of steps (indexed) and their texts,
  * normalized ingredient text and aliases (if the linker generates aliases),
  * and the deterministic assignment results.

Recommended approach (safe by design):

* Only apply LLM suggestions to ingredients that are currently *unassigned*.
* If you later decide to override assigned links, require:

  * a very low deterministic confidence signal, and
  * an explicit, tested rule that prevents duplication regressions.

LLM task input (keep prompts small):

* recipe title (if available)
* steps: list of `{index, text}` (truncate overly long steps if needed)
* one ingredient’s:

  * original ingredient line (`raw_text`), plus
  * parsed ingredient core (`raw_ingredient_text`) and aliases if available

LLM output schema (step link repair v1):

* `ingredient_line_index`: integer
* `step_indices`: list of integers (length 1–3)
* `split_fractions`: optional list of numbers (same length as step_indices; sums to ~1.0)
* `reason`: string (debug only)

Validation rules:

* step indices must be in range.
* max 3 steps.
* if split fractions provided:

  * same length as step indices,
  * each fraction > 0,
  * sum within [0.98, 1.02].

Artifacts:

* `data/output/<run_ts>/rawArtifacts/llm/step_link_repairs.jsonl` with analogous fields to ingredient repairs.

### Milestone 4 — CLI/config wiring + reporting

Goal: make LLM repair strictly opt-in, reproducible, and observable.

What exists at the end:

* `cookimport stage ...` (and any relevant entrypoints used by benchmark/prediction runs) can be run with explicit flags enabling repair.
* The per-file conversion report includes an `llm` stats object.

Opt-in gating (recommended double-gate):

* Require both:

  * a CLI flag selecting repairs, and
  * an env var enabling LLM at all.

This prevents accidental enabling in environments where flags may be defaulted.

Proposed CLI flags:

* `--llm-repair off|ingredients|step_link|all` (default: `off`)
* `--llm-cache-dir <path>` (optional)
* `--llm-max-calls-per-recipe N` (optional)
* `--llm-model <model>` (optional)
* `--llm-dryrun` (optional; never calls network, but still writes “would-have-called” artifacts)

Proposed env vars (names may be adjusted to match repo conventions):

* `COOKIMPORT_LLM_ENABLED=0|1` (default 0)
* `COOKIMPORT_LLM_API_KEY` (required if enabled and not dry-run)
* `COOKIMPORT_LLM_MODEL` (default to a known JSON-capable model)
* `COOKIMPORT_LLM_BASE_URL` (optional; for OpenAI-compatible endpoints)
* `COOKIMPORT_LLM_TIMEOUT_SECS` (default 30)
* `COOKIMPORT_LLM_MAX_RETRIES` (default 2)
* `COOKIMPORT_LLM_CACHE_DIR` (default: `data/output/.cache/llm`)

Reporting:

* Extend the per-file conversion report (the JSON written at run root) to include:

  * `llm: { calls, cache_hits, failures, repairs_applied, seconds_total, tasks: {...} }`

Where `tasks` can break down counts by `ingredient_repair_v1` and `step_link_repair_v1`.

### Milestone 5 — Tests + benchmark iteration

Goal: prove safety and value with deterministic tests and measured evaluation deltas.

What exists at the end:

* Unit tests cover:

  * schema validation rejects bad outputs and falls back safely,
  * cache prevents repeat provider calls for same key,
  * gating prevents calls when disabled,
  * step-link repair only applies to unassigned ingredients (by default rule),
  * dry-run mode never calls network.

* A benchmark comparison exists in **Artifacts and Notes**:

  * baseline (LLM off) vs ingredients repair on vs all on.

Test strategy notes:

* Never call real LLM providers in unit tests.
* Use a fake provider implementation that returns fixed JSON payloads.
* Add at least one regression-style unit test that demonstrates a real improvement pattern (for example, a tricky ingredient line that deterministic parsing misreads but your repair schema + patch logic can fix).

Benchmark strategy:

* Run the golden-set workflow with:

  * LLM OFF
  * LLM ON (ingredients only)
  * LLM ON (ingredients + step_link)

* Compare:

  * `eval_report.json` and `eval_report.md`
  * `missed_gold_spans.jsonl`
  * `false_positive_preds.jsonl`

Tune:

* Adjust thresholds and prompts only after you have artifact evidence (from the JSONLs) for why repairs were rejected or harmful.
* Record threshold/prompt changes in the Decision Log with dates.

## Concrete Steps

All commands below assume you are at the repository root.

1. Baseline stage run (LLM is off by default):

   cookimport stage data/input/<YOUR_GOLDEN_SET_SOURCE_OR_FOLDER>

Then locate the run folder created under `data/output/<timestamp>/` and note:

* `<run_root>/<workbook_slug>.excel_import_report.json`

2. Baseline Label Studio benchmark (only if that is your standard golden-set metric source):

   cookimport labelstudio-benchmark --allow-labelstudio-write

Notes:

* This command is upload-first in non-interactive mode.
* Its artifacts live under `data/golden/...` and should include `eval_report.json` and `eval_report.md`.
* It may also write “prediction-run” artifacts co-located under the eval output directory.

3. After implementing LLM repair, run staging with repair enabled (example):

   export COOKIMPORT_LLM_ENABLED=1
   export COOKIMPORT_LLM_API_KEY="<your key>"
   export COOKIMPORT_LLM_MODEL="<your model>"

   cookimport stage data/input/<YOUR_GOLDEN_SET_SOURCE_OR_FOLDER> --llm-repair ingredients

4. After implementing step-link repair:

   cookimport stage data/input/<YOUR_GOLDEN_SET_SOURCE_OR_FOLDER> --llm-repair all

5. Run tests:

   pytest -q

Expected outcomes:

* Tests pass.
* When LLM repair is enabled, the run folder contains:

  * `data/output/<run_ts>/rawArtifacts/llm/ingredient_repairs.jsonl`
  * optionally `data/output/<run_ts>/rawArtifacts/llm/step_link_repairs.jsonl`

## Validation and Acceptance

This work is accepted when all of the following are true:

1. Deterministic default preserved:

* Running `cookimport stage ...` with no new flags produces the same outputs as before (no LLM calls, no repaired outputs).

2. Safe opt-in behavior:

* With `--llm-repair=ingredients` but `COOKIMPORT_LLM_ENABLED=0`, the pipeline does not call the network and reports “LLM disabled” in logs/stats (repairs are not applied).
* With `COOKIMPORT_LLM_ENABLED=1` and `--llm-repair=ingredients`, LLM calls occur only for gated low-confidence lines and are capped per recipe.

3. Cache and replay:

* Re-running the same command with the same inputs and cache dir produces cache hits and does not re-call the provider for previously seen keys.

4. Strict validation and fallback:

* Invalid JSON, schema mismatches, or invariant violations never crash staging; they produce a “repair rejected” record and fall back to deterministic results.

5. Observable reporting:

* The per-file conversion report JSON includes an `llm` section with counts and seconds.
* The run folder contains the JSONL repair artifacts as described.

6. Measured quality impact:

* On your existing golden set, the “LLM ON (ingredients)” run shows a measurable improvement in at least one ingredient-relevant metric in `eval_report.json` / `eval_report.md`, and does not introduce an unacceptable wave of false positives (document what “unacceptable” means for your use case).
* Step-link repair improves unmatched/incorrect linking cases without reintroducing duplication regressions (confirm via eval artifacts and at least one targeted unit test).

## Idempotence and Recovery

* Cache files are safe to delete; deletion only causes re-calls on the next enabled run.
* Repair JSONLs are purely diagnostic artifacts; deletion does not affect correctness.
* If you hit rate limits or provider instability, set `--llm-repair off` (or `COOKIMPORT_LLM_ENABLED=0`) and rerun to get deterministic outputs.
* Label Studio write operations remain gated by `--allow-labelstudio-write`; do not run benchmark/import commands “just to peek” unless you intend to upload.

## Artifacts and Notes

Fill these in as you execute the plan:

* Baseline eval output dir (LLM OFF): `...`
* Ingredients repair eval output dir (LLM ON): `...`
* All repair eval output dir (LLM ON): `...`

Record a short summary here (example format):

* Baseline vs Ingredients:

  * Key metric deltas: …
  * Notable reductions in missed spans: …
  * Notable new false positives (if any): …

* Ingredients vs All:

  * Step-link improvements observed: …
  * Any regressions and how they were mitigated: …

## Interfaces and Dependencies

### Modules/files expected to be touched

* `cookimport/llm/` — implement real client/provider abstraction, cache, schemas, stats
* `cookimport/parsing/ingredients.py` — add gated repair pass after deterministic parse
* `cookimport/parsing/step_ingredients.py` — add gated repair pass for unmatched/low-confidence
* `cookimport/cli.py` (or wherever `cookimport stage` flags live) — add flags and wire config through
* Conversion report model / writer (where `<workbook_slug>.excel_import_report.json` is generated) — add `llm` stats field
* `tests/` — add deterministic unit tests for cache, gating, and validation

### External dependencies

* Prefer not adding new dependencies if existing ones suffice.
* Use Pydantic v2 for schema validation.
* For HTTP provider calls, prefer existing HTTP client dependency if present; otherwise `requests` is acceptable.
* Do not add any dependency that forces an LLM provider at import time when LLM is disabled.

## Footguns to Avoid (read before implementing)

* Do not enable LLM repair by default. “It works on my machine” defaults are the fastest way to create silent regressions.
* Do not accept “almost JSON” output. If you don’t validate strictly, you will eventually apply a malformed repair and corrupt downstream invariants.
* Don’t let the LLM rewrite the input line. Require `raw_text` to match exactly, or you’ll drift provenance/traceability.
* Watch out for parallelism: split jobs / multi-worker runs can cause duplicate provider calls without a lock. Atomic cache writes prevent corruption but not duplication.
* Remember Label Studio benchmark is upload-first in non-interactive mode. Always use `--allow-labelstudio-write` intentionally.
* Don’t assume old URN namespaces or old docs about output paths/timestamps are correct; verify current emitted IDs and file paths in the repo before hard-coding expectations.

Revised using the concrete repo/documented paths for stage outputs + conversion reports + perf history CSV , the stage output layout + `.job_parts` split-job nuance , Label Studio benchmark/eval artifact layout + timestamp format footgun , and ExecPlan formatting requirements (no nested code fences; omit ``` in a plan-only .md file) .

# Add a lifetime stats dashboard for cookimport (imports + golden-set benchmarks)

This ExecPlan is a living document. The sections `Progress`, `Surprises & Discoveries`, `Decision Log`, and `Outcomes & Retrospective` must be kept up to date as work proceeds.

This plan must be maintained in accordance with `docs/PLANS.md` (ExecPlan requirements and workflow rules).

## Purpose / Big Picture

After this change, a user can generate a single, static “lifetime stats” dashboard (offline, local-only) summarizing:

* **Stage/import runs**: throughput and quality signals across all historical staged files (recipes/tips counts, runtime, derived rates, warnings/errors).
* **Golden-set benchmark runs**: how parsing quality metrics (precision/recall and other eval signals) trend over time across Label Studio evaluations.

The primary user-visible behavior is:

* Running a single CLI command generates a dashboard directory containing `index.html` plus local assets, and the dashboard renders correctly when opened in a browser via `file://...`.
* The dashboard clearly answers: “How fast are imports trending?”, “What are the slowest runs and why?”, “How are benchmark scores moving over time?”, and “Are there obvious regressions in warnings/errors/coverage?”

### Non-goals (v1)

* No web server, no network calls, no external CDNs.
* No attempt to re-run imports or benchmarks; the dashboard is a read-only view over artifacts already on disk.
* No requirement to open or parse full recipe outputs; prefer summarized metric surfaces.

## Progress

* [ ] (2026-02-12) Choose a stable “run record” schema for dashboard data and document it in-code (Pydantic models).
* [ ] (2026-02-12) Implement collectors for:

  * [ ] stage/import history (prefer `data/output/.history/performance_history.csv`; fallback to scanning `*.excel_import_report.json`).
  * [ ] benchmark/eval history (scan `eval_report.json` + optional `coverage.json` / `manifest.json`).
* [ ] (2026-02-12) Implement dashboard generator:

  * [ ] write `dashboard_data.json`
  * [ ] write `index.html`, `assets/dashboard.js`, `assets/style.css` (no external dependencies)
  * [ ] add basic filtering + drill-down links
* [ ] (2026-02-12) Add tests (collector parsing, aggregation correctness, HTML/data output presence) with small fixtures.
* [ ] (2026-02-12) Add documentation for the new command, where it reads from, and how to interpret key charts/tables.
