## Decision Log

(Keep this section updated during implementation.)

* Decision: Prefer existing “small” metric surfaces (`performance_history.csv` and `eval_report.json`) as the primary data sources; only scan `*.excel_import_report.json` as a fallback when history CSV is missing or incomplete.
  Rationale: Avoid reading huge recipe outputs and reduce I/O and runtime for dashboard generation; reuse the repo’s existing normalized metrics.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-12 / plan revision

* Decision: Treat benchmark “prediction runs” as a distinct run category and avoid double-counting them as normal stage imports.
  Rationale: Label Studio workflows can produce stage-like outputs under `data/output/.../labelstudio/...` and/or under `<eval_output_dir>/prediction-run/`; counting them as normal imports will skew “lifetime import” stats and confuse users.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-12 / plan revision

## Outcomes & Retrospective

(Write entries here at the end of each milestone or at completion.)

## Context and Orientation

This repository produces multiple “metric surfaces” on disk. The dashboard should read those surfaces (preferably the already-normalized ones), aggregate them, and render a static HTML view.

### Key artifact surfaces (current, code-verified)

1. **Per-file conversion report** (stage/import health + timing)

Each staged source file writes a report JSON at:

* `data/output/<YYYY-MM-DD_HH.MM.SS>/<workbook_slug>.excel_import_report.json`

These reports include (at least) counts, warnings/errors, confidence aggregates, timing, and output footprint. Key fields called out in docs include:

* volume counts (`totalRecipes`, `totalTips`, `totalTipCandidates`, `totalTopicCandidates`)
* data health (`missingFieldCounts`, `skippedRows`, `lowConfidenceSheets`, `warnings`, `errors`)
* runtime timing (`timing.total_seconds`, `timing.parsing_seconds`, `timing.writing_seconds`, `timing.ocr_seconds`, plus checkpoints)
* output footprint (`outputStats.files`, `outputStats.largestFiles`)

2. **Cross-run performance history CSV** (small, lifetime-trendable)

* `data/output/.history/performance_history.csv`

This is generated from the per-file `*.excel_import_report.json` reports. It is already normalized to “one row per imported file,” and includes derived metrics like per-recipe/per-tip seconds and outlier flags. This should be the primary source for stage/import trend charts, because it is compact and intentionally designed for “lifetime history”.

3. **Label Studio benchmark/eval artifacts** (golden-set quality metrics)

Evaluation commands emit artifacts including:

* `eval_report.json`
* `eval_report.md`
* `missed_gold_spans.jsonl`
* `false_positive_preds.jsonl`

Label Studio ingestion can also emit:

* `coverage.json` (e.g., `extracted_chars`, `chunked_chars`, `warnings`)
* `manifest.json` (includes task upload counts and metadata)

Benchmark runs are commonly stored under:

* `data/golden/eval-vs-pipeline/<timestamp>/`

…and benchmark prediction artifacts may be co-located under:

* `<eval_output_dir>/prediction-run/`

### Output layout facts that matter for the dashboard (to avoid footguns)

* Run timestamp folders are dot-separated in the time portion: `%Y-%m-%d_%H.%M.%S`. Do not assume `:` is used.
* Stage outputs include intermediate/final drafts, tips, chunks, raw artifacts, and a report JSON at the run root. Do not assume a `reports/` subfolder.
* Split-job staging (PDF/EPUB) may create temporary artifacts under:

  * `data/output/.job_parts/<workbook_slug>/job_<index>/raw/...`
    These should be ignored by the dashboard unless explicitly debugging a failed merge; they are not “final runs”.

### Dashboard terms (define once and use consistently)

* **Stage file record**: one imported source file as represented by one row in `performance_history.csv` (or one `*.excel_import_report.json` when falling back).
* **Benchmark eval record**: one Label Studio evaluation run represented by one `eval_report.json` (optionally enriched by `coverage.json` / `manifest.json` in the same folder).
* **Run category**: a label used only by the dashboard to prevent mixing apples and oranges (e.g., `stage_import`, `labelstudio_import`, `benchmark_eval`, `benchmark_prediction`).

## Plan of Work

### Milestone 1: Inventory + stable data model (schema first)

At the end of this milestone, there is a clear, code-backed schema for what the dashboard consumes, and the schema is grounded in the existing on-disk metric surfaces. A novice can read the schema and understand what data is expected and where it comes from.

Work:

1. Create a small “dashboard schema” module using Pydantic v2 models.

   Suggested location (align with existing perf analytics code paths):

   * `cookimport/analytics/dashboard_schema.py`

   Define a top-level model like:

   * `DashboardData`

     * `generated_at` (ISO string)
     * `output_root` (string, default `data/output`)
     * `golden_root` (string, default `data/golden`)
     * `stage_records: list[StageRecord]`
     * `benchmark_records: list[BenchmarkRecord]`
     * `summary: DashboardSummary` (pre-aggregated totals, optional)

   Where:

   * `StageRecord` is designed to be directly populated from one CSV row (preferred) or from one conversion report (fallback).
   * `BenchmarkRecord` is designed to be populated from `eval_report.json` (and optionally coverage/manifest).

2. Be explicit about which fields are optional vs required.

   The dashboard must not “invent zeros” for missing metrics. Use `None` for missing numeric fields and omit those points from charts.

3. Record “source pointers” on each record so the UI can link/drill down without needing to load huge data:

   * `artifact_dir` (relative path from repo root if possible)
   * `report_path` (path to the CSV row source or JSON report)
   * `run_timestamp` (parsed from folder name or report field; store both raw + parsed if needed)

4. Add a small `schema_version` string to `DashboardData` so future iterations can change fields safely.

Acceptance:

* A developer can read `dashboard_schema.py` and know exactly what dashboard data looks like and which disk artifacts populate it.
* There is a tiny unit test that can instantiate `DashboardData` from minimal synthetic dicts.

### Milestone 2: Collectors (read-only, robust, skip footguns)

At the end of this milestone, running a Python function can scan local outputs and produce a populated `DashboardData` instance without errors, even when some runs are partial/missing.

Work:

1. Implement stage/import collector:

   Suggested module:

   * `cookimport/analytics/dashboard_collect.py`

   Behavior:

   * Prefer reading `data/output/.history/performance_history.csv` if present.
   * If it is missing, empty, or the user passes a flag like `--scan-reports`, fall back to scanning:

     * `data/output/<timestamp>/*.excel_import_report.json`
   * Never read:

     * `data/output/.job_parts/**`
     * any `prediction-run/**` directories (if they are under a searched root)
   * For each stage record, attempt to classify `run_category`:

     * If the artifact path indicates Label Studio ingestion (`.../labelstudio/...`), mark as `labelstudio_import` (and default it to hidden in the “Stage imports” view unless the user enables it).
     * Otherwise mark as `stage_import`.

   Implementation notes:

   * Do not assume CSV columns beyond what exists; load header dynamically and map known column names.
   * If derived metrics are missing (e.g., seconds-per-recipe), compute them only when numerator and denominator are present and denominator > 0.
   * Guard division-by-zero and “infinite” rates; store `None` instead.

2. Implement benchmark collector:

   * Scan for `eval_report.json` under `golden_root`, with a priority on `data/golden/eval-vs-pipeline/*/eval_report.json` but also allow nested patterns for other eval outputs.
   * For each eval directory:

     * Parse `eval_report.json` into a normalized `BenchmarkRecord`.
     * If present, read `coverage.json` and compute coverage ratio `chunked_chars / extracted_chars` (store as optional float).
     * If present, read `manifest.json` and capture task counts (optional fields).

   Classification:

   * Records from directories containing `eval_report.json` are `benchmark_eval`.
   * Do not treat `prediction-run` conversion outputs as benchmark eval; if you choose to surface them at all, treat them as `benchmark_prediction` and keep them separate from “stage imports”.

3. Add “collector resilience” rules:

   * If a JSON file is malformed, skip that record, add a warning to a `collector_warnings` list in `DashboardData` (optional), and continue.
   * If a directory name looks like a timestamp but fails parse, keep the raw string and sort such runs last (stable ordering).

Acceptance:

* A unit test can run collectors against a temp directory containing:

  * a tiny `performance_history.csv`
  * one fake `*.excel_import_report.json`
  * one fake `eval_report.json` (+ optional coverage/manifest)
    and returns `DashboardData` with correctly classified records.

### Milestone 3: Static HTML dashboard (one command)

At the end of this milestone, running a `cookimport` CLI command generates a static dashboard directory containing `index.html` plus local assets, and the dashboard renders correctly when opened in a browser via `file://...`.

Work:

1. Add a new CLI command (Typer) to generate the dashboard:

   * Command name: `cookimport stats-dashboard`
   * Flags (keep minimal; add more only if truly needed):

     * `--output-root` (default: `data/output`)
     * `--golden-root` (default: `data/golden`)
     * `--out-dir` (default: `data/output/.history/dashboard`)
     * `--open` (boolean; if true, open the generated HTML in the default browser)
     * `--since-days` (optional; limit to recent runs for faster generation)
     * `--scan-reports` (boolean; force scanning `*.excel_import_report.json` in addition to/without relying on performance_history.csv)

   The command should:

   * collect data
   * optionally aggregate summary
   * write dashboard files
   * print the path to `index.html`

2. Implement HTML generation with a separation of concerns:

   Output layout:

   * `<out-dir>/index.html`
   * `<out-dir>/assets/style.css`
   * `<out-dir>/assets/dashboard.js`
   * `<out-dir>/assets/dashboard_data.json`

   Requirements:

   * No external CDN dependencies.
   * `dashboard.js` loads `dashboard_data.json` and renders charts/tables client-side.
   * Keep JS minimal. Prefer simple SVG-based sparklines or very small custom charting over introducing a heavy library.

3. UI structure goals for v1 (readable, boring, useful)

   Header:

   * Generated timestamp
   * Data roots used
   * Totals (number of stage records, benchmark records, total recipes, total runtime seconds where available)

   Throughput section:

   * Trend of seconds-per-recipe over time (only for runs where recipe count > 0 and time is present)
   * A table of slowest runs (by total seconds) with artifact paths displayed and clickable local links when possible

   Benchmarks section:

   * Trend of recall/precision (and F1 if available) over time, grouped by eval scope if present
   * A table of recent benchmarks (timestamp, source identifier if present, key metrics, link to eval folder, link to eval_report.md if present)

   Filters:

   * Run category toggles (stage_import vs benchmark_eval; allow enabling labelstudio_import / benchmark_prediction as opt-in)
   * Importer/source filters (dropdown populated from data)
   * Date range presets (7/30/90 days)

4. Rendering robustness

   * Missing metrics: omit from charts rather than showing zero.
   * No benchmark data: hide the benchmark section with a friendly note.
   * Path links: if you can safely create relative links from `out-dir` to artifact dirs, do so; otherwise display absolute paths and add a “copy” button in JS.

Acceptance:

* Running the command produces the output files and opening `index.html` shows tables and at least one trend visualization when data exists.
* Links do not 404 when using default directory layouts.

### Milestone 4: Tests, docs, and hardening

At the end of this milestone, dashboard generation is covered by tests that run in CI without requiring real cookbooks or Label Studio. Documentation tells a novice how to generate the dashboard and what questions it answers.

Work:

1. Add fixtures for testing collectors:

   * A tiny `performance_history.csv` fixture with a handful of representative rows/columns.
   * A minimal `*.excel_import_report.json` fixture capturing the key fields used by the fallback scanner.
   * A minimal benchmark fixture directory containing:

     * `eval_report.json`
     * optionally `coverage.json` and `manifest.json`

   Keep these fixtures tiny and synthetic; they should not contain large recipe bodies.

2. Add unit tests:

   * Stage collector: parses CSV, computes derived fields safely (no division by zero), classifies run categories.
   * Benchmark collector: parses eval report, reads optional coverage/manifest, classifies.
   * Generator: writes expected files to a temp directory; `dashboard_data.json` validates against `DashboardData` schema.

3. Add a short doc:

   * Where to place: `docs/08-analytics/` or `docs/02-cli/` (choose the existing convention)
   * Include:

     * command usage
     * where it reads from (`data/output/.history/performance_history.csv`, `data/golden/**/eval_report.json`)
     * how to interpret the key charts/tables
     * common pitfalls (see below)

4. Hardening checklist (non-Progress narrative, but ensure it is done)

   * Ensure dashboard generation is idempotent: re-running overwrites only files under `out-dir`.
   * Ensure collectors never write into `data/output` or `data/golden` (read-only).
   * Ensure timestamp parsing matches dot-separated time format.
   * Ensure `.job_parts` is ignored.
   * Ensure benchmark prediction artifacts don’t get counted as normal stage imports.

Acceptance:

* CI can run tests without external services.
* A novice can run the command and understand what they are looking at.

## Concrete Steps

(These are the “do this now” instructions for an implementer; update them as work proceeds.)

1. Find existing CLI wiring and mirror patterns.

   From repo root:

   ls cookimport
   rg "perf-report" cookimport/cli.py cookimport -n
   rg "Typer" cookimport/cli.py -n

2. Implement schema + collectors.

   From repo root (examples; adjust to repo tooling):

   python -m pytest -q

3. Generate dashboard locally.

   From repo root:

   cookimport stats-dashboard

   Expected console output should include something like:

   Wrote dashboard to data/output/.history/dashboard
   Open this file in your browser:
   data/output/.history/dashboard/index.html

   If `--open` is passed, it should attempt to open the HTML file.

## Validation and Acceptance

Acceptance is met when all of the following are true:

* Running `cookimport stats-dashboard` on a machine with existing `data/output` and/or `data/golden` artifacts produces:

  * `data/output/.history/dashboard/index.html`
  * `data/output/.history/dashboard/assets/dashboard_data.json`
  * `data/output/.history/dashboard/assets/dashboard.js`
  * `data/output/.history/dashboard/assets/style.css`

* Opening `index.html` via `file://...` shows:

  * stage/import totals and at least one trend plot when stage history exists,
  * benchmark section when `eval_report.json` exists under `golden_root`,
  * a slowest-runs table with correct artifact paths,
  * filters that hide/show categories without errors.

* Tests pass, and the collectors handle missing/malformed records by skipping them (with a warning) rather than failing the whole run.

## Idempotence and Recovery

* The dashboard command must be safe to run repeatedly.
* It must only write inside `--out-dir` (default `data/output/.history/dashboard`).
* If some artifacts are malformed (partial run, truncated JSON), the generator must:

  * skip that record,
  * record/log a warning,
  * still produce a dashboard from the remaining valid data.

If the user reports “dashboard is empty”, the recovery path should be:

* Confirm `data/output/.history/performance_history.csv` exists; if not, run:

  cookimport perf-report

  then rerun:

  cookimport stats-dashboard

* Confirm there are `eval_report.json` files under `data/golden/`; if not, run an eval workflow first.

## Artifacts and Notes

Common pitfalls to explicitly guard against:

* Timestamp parsing mismatch: folders use `%Y-%m-%d_%H.%M.%S` (dots in time). If you parse with colons, sorting/grouping will break.
* Double-counting benchmark predictions:

  * benchmark eval directories may contain `prediction-run/`
  * labelstudio ingestion outputs may live under `data/output/<timestamp>/labelstudio/...`
    These should not inflate stage/import lifetime stats unless explicitly enabled as separate categories.
* Split-job temporary artifacts:

  * ignore `data/output/.job_parts/**` unless intentionally debugging merges
  * do not treat job parts as completed runs

When adding new derived metrics, always do “safe math”:

* If denominator is 0 or missing, record `None`, not `0` or `Infinity`.

## Interfaces and Dependencies

### Python modules to add (suggested)

* `cookimport/analytics/dashboard_schema.py`

  * Pydantic models for `DashboardData`, `StageRecord`, `BenchmarkRecord`, etc.

* `cookimport/analytics/dashboard_collect.py`

  * `collect_dashboard_data(output_root: Path, golden_root: Path, since_days: int | None, scan_reports: bool) -> DashboardData`

* `cookimport/analytics/dashboard_render.py`

  * `render_dashboard(out_dir: Path, data: DashboardData) -> Path` returning `index.html` path

### CLI interface to add

In `cookimport/cli.py` (or wherever Typer commands are registered), add:

* `stats-dashboard` command

  * calls collectors + renderer
  * writes outputs
  * optionally opens browser

Do not add external JS/CSS dependencies. Keep all assets local.

---

Plan revision note (2026-02-12): Updated the ExecPlan to use the repo’s documented metric surfaces and concrete artifact layouts (conversion reports, `performance_history.csv`, `eval_report.json`), clarified timestamp format and split-job/benchmark prediction footguns, and tightened the “read-only collector” approach to avoid scanning huge outputs or double-counting Label Studio prediction artifacts.
```

## docs/plans/OGplans/I2.1 Tighten the benchmark-driven improv.md

```markdown
---
summary: "Archived original ExecPlan for benchmark-loop tightening and offline iteration."
read_when:
  - When reviewing historical benchmark architecture decisions
  - When tracing why current bench suite contracts look the way they do
---

# Tighten the benchmark-driven improvement loop for cookimport parsing (freeform golden sets)

This ExecPlan is a living document. The sections `Progress`, `Surprises & Discoveries`, `Decision Log`, and `Outcomes & Retrospective` must be kept up to date as work proceeds.

Maintain this document in accordance with `docs/PLANS.md`, which defines the required ExecPlan format and workflow rules.

## Purpose / Big Picture

After this change, a developer (or AI coding agent) can improve the EPUB/PDF parsing pipeline in fast, repeatable iterations using **existing freeform golden sets**, without needing Label Studio running and without needing to understand Label Studio internals.

The user-visible proof is a tight loop that works end-to-end with one command:

* Run an **offline** benchmark suite against freeform gold exports.
* Receive a machine-readable report plus an **iteration packet** (ranked examples + context + “why” signals + failure mode summaries + tunable knobs involved).
* Make a code or config change, rerun, and immediately see what improved/regressed and why.

A secondary proof is spend-awareness: each run quantifies “how many LLM repair calls would happen” under current thresholds (no paid calls), with estimated tokens/cost, so the fastest wins come from reducing noise and duplication before turning on any real LLM repair.

## Progress

* [x] (2026-02-12 16:50Z) Revised ExecPlan to align with current Label Studio export/eval contracts and to call out known footguns explicitly.
* [ ] (2026-02-12 17:00Z) Baseline: run current freeform eval on one known gold export + existing pred-run and record artifact schema + metrics we will preserve.
* [ ] (2026-02-12 17:00Z) Add an explicit **non-interactive offline benchmark** path (no upload, no LS env vars) that generates a pred-run locally and then runs freeform eval.
* [ ] (2026-02-12 17:00Z) Add a small **bench suite manifest** (dev/test) that maps sources to freeform gold exports and per-item eval options.
* [ ] (2026-02-12 17:00Z) Add a suite runner that writes deterministic run artifacts and an aggregate report.
* [ ] (2026-02-12 17:00Z) Add an **iteration packet** generator that turns eval outputs into agent-friendly diagnostics (top failures + context + “why” signals + suggested knobs).
* [ ] (2026-02-12 17:00Z) Add optional **decision tracing** for segmentation/chunking so failures can be explained in terms of rule/threshold reasons.
* [ ] (2026-02-12 17:00Z) Add a **knob/config** mechanism that makes safe tuning easy and records effective values in run artifacts.
* [ ] (2026-02-12 17:00Z) Add a deterministic **parameter sweep** tool for cheap local autotuning on the dev suite.
* [ ] (2026-02-12 17:00Z) Add/validate **noise reduction** primitives (dedupe + consolidation + gating) and measure impact on prediction volume and cost model.
* [ ] (2026-02-12 17:00Z) Add a structured **LLM escalation queue emitter + token/cost estimator** (counting only; no paid calls).
* [ ] (2026-02-12 17:00Z) Add tests and documentation so a novice can run the loop and interpret outputs without Label Studio.

## Surprises & Discoveries

(Keep this updated during implementation.)

* Observation: …
  Evidence: …

## Decision Log

* Decision: The benchmark loop will be built on top of the **existing freeform export + eval contracts** (freeform spans + segment manifest; eval outputs including missed/false-positive JSONL), rather than inventing a parallel scoring format.
  Rationale: This avoids schema drift and preserves continuity with existing golden sets and evaluation logic. It also makes offline benchmarking a “thin wrapper” around proven components.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-12 / ExecPlan author

* Decision: Add an explicit **non-interactive offline** benchmark path (suite-capable) that does not upload and does not require Label Studio credentials.
  Rationale: Current CLI benchmark behavior is upload-first; many users expect “benchmark” to be scoring-only. Offline iteration is the fastest path for heuristic improvement and is safer by default.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-12 / ExecPlan author

* Decision: Matching/scoring will remain **chunking-invariant** by default for freeform gold: use touched block index sets (or their overlap) as the stable coordinate system.
  Rationale: Freeform gold intentionally does not mirror internal chunk boundaries. Scoring should reward “picked it up in the right region,” while still optionally reporting boundary quality as a secondary metric.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-12 / ExecPlan author

* Decision: Precision will be reported with explicit caveats and additional “prediction density/noise” metrics.
  Rationale: Unlabeled regions in freeform gold are not guaranteed negatives. Treating all unlabeled text as negative makes precision misleading; density and “suspected FP” diagnostics are more actionable for cost control.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-12 / ExecPlan author

* Decision: Suite runs will default to writing under `data/golden/bench/…` (not a new top-level `data/bench/…`) and will reuse the project’s timestamp folder format.
  Rationale: Golden/eval artifacts already live under `data/golden`; keeping benchmark artifacts adjacent reduces path confusion and keeps “labeling/eval/bench” in one place.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-12 / ExecPlan author

## Outcomes & Retrospective

(Add entries at milestone completion.)

## Context and Orientation

### What this repo does (relevant slice)

`cookimport` ingests recipes from EPUB/PDF (and other formats) by extracting a linear stream of text **blocks**, enriching them with **signals** (heading-ness, ingredient-likeness, etc.), segmenting them into recipe/tip candidates, and then writing structured outputs.

### Key terms (use these consistently)

* Block: The smallest stable text unit used for extraction and evaluation (roughly a paragraph/list/header line). Blocks are ordered and have indices `0..N-1` within a source. Block indices are the stable coordinate system for freeform evaluation.
* Pipeline predictions: The spans/ranges/chunks the pipeline believes correspond to labeled structures (recipe title, ingredient lines, instruction lines, tips, etc.). Internally this may be represented as candidates or tasks; for benchmarking we treat them as labeled block ranges/sets.
* Freeform gold span: A human-highlighted span (in Label Studio) with a label. In export, each gold span is mapped to the set of block indices it touches (directly or via a segment manifest mapping offsets back to blocks).
* Segment manifest: A JSONL mapping that ties uploaded “segment text” offsets back to original block indices so span highlights can be evaluated in block space.
* Suite item: One benchmark case mapping (source file + freeform gold export + per-item options like force-source-match).

### Where the relevant code lives today

Label Studio workflows are implemented under `cookimport/labelstudio/`:

* `ingest.py`: extraction + task generation + (optionally) upload + run artifacts
* `export.py`: export shaping to JSONL golden sets (including freeform spans + segment manifest)
* `eval_freeform.py`: freeform evaluation and report artifacts
* tests under `tests/test_labelstudio_*.py`

The offline benchmark loop in this plan must reuse the **existing export/eval contracts** and should reuse ingestion/task generation where possible, but must not require the Label Studio server when running offline.

### Current behavior that motivates this plan

* The non-interactive CLI benchmark path is currently **upload-first**: it runs a prediction import/upload before scoring. This is surprising to many users and blocks offline iteration.
* Freeform eval can collapse to near-zero matches if source identity mismatches or if split-job block-index rebasing is broken.
* Freeform labels and ID prefixes have had historical drift; eval normalizes some legacy labels, but any new tooling must not reintroduce drift.

### Known footguns to avoid (and how this plan prevents them)

1. “Benchmark” accidentally uploads or needs LS credentials.

   * Fix: offline mode must never initialize the Label Studio client and must not require `LABEL_STUDIO_URL/API_KEY`. Upload remains gated behind explicit consent and a separate flag/path.

2. Near-zero overlap due to source mismatch.

   * Fix: suite items must carry a `force_source_match` boolean, default false. When false, runs should fail fast with a clear error when the source identity/hash doesn’t match the gold export’s recorded identity. When true, record that override prominently in reports.

3. Near-zero overlap due to split-job merge index rebasing regression.

   * Fix: offline pred-run generation must reuse the same merge/rebase logic as stage/import paths. Add a regression test that a split-run produces globally increasing block indices and that eval overlap is non-trivially > 0 on a known fixture.

4. Misleading precision due to unlabeled ≠ negative in freeform gold.

   * Fix: emphasize recall/coverage and add “prediction density” and “suspected FP” diagnostics instead of pretending unlabeled blocks are ground-truth negatives.

5. Timestamp/path drift causing “where did my outputs go?” confusion.

   * Fix: write everything under a single predictable root (`data/golden/bench/...`) and include `suite_used.json` and absolute/relative paths in manifests.

6. ID/URN prefix drift (`urn:cookimport:*` vs `urn:recipeimport:*` historical confusion).

   * Fix: do not hardcode ID prefixes in new code. Parse and propagate whatever IDs the current ingestion code emits; only key off stable fields (source hash, block index, deterministic item IDs).

## Plan of Work

This plan is organized as milestones that each produce a verifiable, working outcome. The story is:

* Make offline benchmarking possible without Label Studio.
* Make it suite-capable and deterministic.
* Make outputs actionable for autonomous iteration (iteration packet).
* Then add tuning tooling (knobs + sweep) and cost-aware noise reduction.

### Milestone 0: Baseline reality check (preserve what already works)

At the end of this milestone, you can point to exactly what artifacts and metrics exist today and what the offline loop must preserve.

Work:

* Identify at least one existing freeform export (it should include `exports/freeform_span_labels.jsonl` and `exports/freeform_segment_manifest.jsonl`).
* Identify at least one existing pred-run folder that freeform eval can consume (a prior labelstudio import/benchmark run).
* Run the existing freeform eval command on that pair and inspect the produced artifacts (JSON + MD + missed/false-positive JSONL).

Proof:

* You can name (in this plan, as an update) the exact filenames produced and the top-level keys in the eval JSON that downstream tooling should rely on.

### Milestone 1: Define a bench suite manifest (dev/test) and validate it

At the end of this milestone, there is a suite manifest format checked into the repo (or stored in a deterministic local path) that enumerates benchmark items and validates inputs.

Suite item fields (minimum):

* `item_id`: stable string ID
* `source_path`: repo-relative path to the input file (EPUB/PDF, etc.)
* `gold_dir`: path to the gold export directory (the folder that contains `exports/…`)
* `force_source_match`: bool (default false)
* optional notes

Suite structure:

* Two manifests: `dev` (iteration) and `test` (held out).

Proof:

* A `cookimport bench validate --suite <path>` command (or equivalent) checks that:

  * source files exist,
  * gold export files exist,
  * required export filenames exist,
  * and the gold export’s recorded source identity matches the provided source (unless forced).

### Milestone 2: Add an explicit offline pred-run builder (no upload, no LS dependency)

At the end of this milestone, the system can generate a “pred-run” folder locally for a given source file without talking to Label Studio, and it is compatible with the existing freeform eval.

Design constraints:

* Must not require Label Studio server or env vars.
* Must not upload anything.
* Must write the same core artifacts that eval expects from a pred-run (for example tasks JSONL and any extracted archive/text it needs for context).

Implementation approach:

* Refactor the ingestion path so “generate tasks + write run artifacts” is separable from “upload tasks”.
* Add a function (or option) like `upload=False` / `offline=True` to the internal runner so CLI can request artifact generation only.
* Ensure this path still honors split-job planning/merge behavior so block indices are in the same global coordinate space as gold.

Proof:

* Running the offline pred-run builder on one suite item produces a pred-run directory.
* Running freeform eval using that pred-run directory and the gold export produces non-empty, sensible metrics and the usual eval artifacts.

### Milestone 3: Offline suite runner with deterministic, reproducible run artifacts

At the end of this milestone, a single command runs the whole dev suite offline and produces a stable run directory containing:

* per-item pred-run artifacts (or references to cached pred-runs),
* per-item eval outputs,
* an aggregate suite report (MD) and metrics (JSON),
* and a copy of the suite manifest used.

Determinism requirements:

* Any randomness (sampling, ordering, sweep seeds) must be removed or seeded and recorded.
* If caching is introduced (recommended), it must be keyed by source content hash + config hash and be safe to delete.

Proof:

* Running the suite twice with the same code/inputs/config produces identical aggregate metrics JSON (ignoring timestamps/paths).
* The run directory contains enough information to reproduce the run later (suite copy + effective config + version info).

### Milestone 4: Iteration packet (make the benchmark “explain itself”)

At the end of this milestone, each suite run produces an `iteration_packet/` designed to be directly consumable by an AI coding agent (or a human) to fix the next most impactful issues.

The packet must include:

* A short summary that highlights:

  * metric deltas vs an optional baseline run,
  * prediction volume/density deltas,
  * top regressions.
* Ranked failure cases with enough context to fix them:

  * missed gold spans,
  * suspected false positives,
  * fragmentation/over-splitting cases (one gold span covered by many tiny preds),
  * “confusion pairs” (pred label A overlaps gold label B).
* For each case, include:

  * the relevant block text context (a small window),
  * the signals/features for those blocks (heading/ingredient-ish/etc.),
  * and where possible the rule/threshold “reason codes” that led to the decision (see next milestone).
* A clear separation between:

  * chunking-invariant coverage metrics (primary for freeform),
  * strict overlap metrics (secondary),
  * and density/noise metrics (primary for cost control).

Proof:

* `iteration_packet/README.md` explains how to use the packet.
* `iteration_packet/cases.jsonl` contains self-contained case records.
* `iteration_packet/top_failures.md` renders the top N cases in a readable way with minimal context needed for a fix.

### Milestone 5: Optional decision tracing for segmentation/chunking (high leverage diagnostics)

At the end of this milestone, the parsing pipeline can run in a “trace” mode that records structured events explaining why spans started/ended, why blocks were classified, and which thresholds were applied.

Requirements:

* Off by default.
* Enabled by a CLI flag (and threaded through worker/split-job runs).
* Written as JSONL (one event per line), diffable and machine-readable.
* Trace events must include a stable correlation key that ties them to predicted spans and block indices.

Proof:

* With trace enabled, a pred-run contains a `traces/<item_id>.trace.jsonl`.
* The iteration packet links trace excerpts to top failure cases.

### Milestone 6: Knob registry + config loader (safe tuning without code hunting)

At the end of this milestone, key thresholds/weights that drive segmentation and classification can be overridden via a config file, with:

* a registry describing each knob (name, type, default, bounds, description),
* a loader that applies overrides,
* and run artifacts that record the effective knob values.

Constraints:

* Prefer to reuse any existing config patterns in the repo (do not introduce a second incompatible config system).
* The knob system should be explicit and safe: bounds checked, unknown keys rejected (or warned loudly).

Proof:

* `cookimport bench run --suite <dev> --config knobs.dev.json` changes outcomes and records effective knobs in the run directory.

### Milestone 7: Deterministic parameter sweep tooling (cheap local autotuning)

At the end of this milestone, there is a tool to try a small grid (or seeded search) of knob values on the dev suite and produce:

* a leaderboard of configs and scores,
* a “best config” file,
* and a confirmation run on the test suite to detect overfitting.

Objective definition (must be explicit in code and in output):

* maximize chunking-invariant coverage on core labels,
* minimize prediction density/noise,
* optionally improve strict overlap as a tie-breaker.

Proof:

* Re-running the sweep with the same seed produces the same best config and leaderboard ordering.

### Milestone 8: Noise reduction primitives + LLM cost estimator (counting only)

At the end of this milestone:

* prediction volumes drop substantially on dev without harming chunking-invariant coverage beyond an explicit tolerance,
* and the run metrics include an LLM escalation/cost section that changes as knobs change.

Implement/validate these primitives if they do not already exist:

* Deduplication: collapse identical/equivalent predicted spans.
* Consolidation: prefer a small set of high-confidence, minimally overlapping spans per label.
* Noise gating: reduce emission of narrative prose as actionable content.

LLM estimator requirements:

* Emit an `llm_escalation_queue.jsonl` (counting only, no calls).
* Estimate tokens using the intended prompt template and context window policy.
* Summarize cost using configurable pricing assumptions.

Proof:

* The suite report shows before/after prediction counts and the estimated cost impact.

### Milestone 9: Tests + docs (novice-proof, regression-proof)

At the end of this milestone, a novice can add a new gold export to the suite and run the loop offline.

Add tests for:

* freeform span → touched blocks mapping invariants (and legacy label normalization),
* offline pred-run generation does not touch Label Studio client code paths,
* split-job merge index rebasing remains correct,
* dedupe/consolidation invariants,
* knob loading and bounds checks.

Docs:

* Add a short runbook in `docs/` that shows:

  * how to create/update a suite,
  * how to run offline bench,
  * how to interpret iteration packet outputs,
  * and how to safely try knob edits/sweeps.

Proof:

* Running the repo test command passes, and the doc includes a minimal “quickstart transcript” with expected output filenames.

## Concrete Steps

All commands below assume repo root as the working directory. Replace runner details (`uv run`, `poetry run`, etc.) with the repo’s standard workflow after inspecting `pyproject.toml`.

1. Install editable and confirm CLI:

   python -m pip install -e .
   cookimport --help
   cookimport labelstudio-eval --help
   cookimport labelstudio-benchmark --help

2. Baseline one known pair (update this plan with what you observe):

   cookimport labelstudio-eval freeform-spans 
   --pred-run <path-to-existing-pred-run> 
   --gold-spans <path-to-gold-dir>/exports/freeform_span_labels.jsonl 
   --output-dir <tmp-eval-out> 
   --force-source-match

3. Create a suite manifest (dev/test) under the agreed root:

   mkdir -p data/golden/bench/suites
   (Create data/golden/bench/suites/dev.json and test.json)

4. Run the new offline suite bench (to be implemented):

   cookimport bench run 
   --suite data/golden/bench/suites/dev.json 
   --out data/golden/bench/runs/

5. Inspect outputs:

   ls data/golden/bench/runs/<timestamp>/
   cat data/golden/bench/runs/<timestamp>/report.md
   ls data/golden/bench/runs/<timestamp>/iteration_packet/

6. Run a sweep (to be implemented):

   cookimport bench sweep 
   --suite data/golden/bench/suites/dev.json 
   --budget 25 
   --out data/golden/bench/sweeps/

7. Validate best config on test:

   cookimport bench run 
   --suite data/golden/bench/suites/test.json 
   --config data/golden/bench/sweeps/<timestamp>/best_config.json 
   --out data/golden/bench/runs/

Expected “success looks like” (example shape; update to match real outputs):

```
report.md includes:
  - per-label coverage metrics
  - prediction density totals
  - fragmentation stats
  - llm_cost_estimate section (counting only)
```

## Validation and Acceptance

Acceptance is behavior, not internal structure.

The work is accepted when:

* Offline benchmark runs end-to-end on the dev suite with one command and produces:

  * an aggregate markdown report,
  * a machine-readable metrics JSON,
  * per-item eval outputs compatible with current freeform eval,
  * and an iteration packet with ranked failure cases including block context and signals.

* Offline truly means offline:

  * No upload occurs.
  * No Label Studio server/env vars are required.
  * The tool fails fast if an upload-required path is attempted without explicit consent.

* Determinism holds:

  * Re-running with identical inputs/config yields identical metrics (ignoring timestamps/paths).

* The iteration packet is sufficient for autonomous iteration:

  * A reasonable engineer can fix at least one top failure by reading only the packet and the codebase (no Label Studio replay required).

* The knob/config system allows safe tuning and is recorded in run artifacts.

* Sweep results are deterministic and include a held-out test confirmation run.

* Tests cover the core matching/mapping logic and the offline pred-run generation path.

## Idempotence and Recovery

This plan must be safe to run repeatedly.

* All outputs are written under `data/golden/bench/…` with timestamped subfolders.
* Deleting a run folder must be sufficient cleanup; caches (if any) must be optional and safe to delete.
* Offline pred-run generation must not mutate gold exports.
* If a run is interrupted, rerunning should either resume safely or start fresh in a new timestamped directory without corrupting prior runs.

## Artifacts and Notes

Standardize outputs so tooling can rely on them:

* data/golden/bench/suites/
  dev.json
  test.json
* data/golden/bench/runs/<timestamp>/
  suite_used.json
  report.md
  metrics.json
  per_item/<item_id>/
  pred_run/                  (offline-generated, eval-compatible)
  eval_freeform/             (existing eval outputs)
  traces/                    (optional)
  iteration_packet/
  README.md
  summary.md
  cases.jsonl
  top_failures.md
  knobs_effective.json
  llm_escalation_queue.jsonl   (counting only)

Keep “packet” files small enough to paste into an AI coding prompt. For large context, reference per-item files and stable IDs instead of dumping entire documents.

## Interfaces and Dependencies

Prefer building on existing modules instead of creating parallel scoring code.

### CLI surface (proposed; adapt to existing CLI conventions)

* cookimport bench run --suite <path> [--config <path>] [--out <dir>] [--trace] [--baseline <run_dir>]
* cookimport bench validate --suite <path>
* cookimport bench sweep --suite <path> [--budget N] [--seed N] [--objective <name>] [--out <dir>]
* cookimport bench cost --suite <path> [--config <path>] [--pricing <path>]

If the project prefers keeping this under the existing labelstudio namespace, implement the same behavior as:

* cookimport labelstudio-benchmark --offline --suite <path> ...

…but ensure the offline mode name is explicit and cannot be confused with upload-first behavior.

### Core functions/modules to add or extend (adapt paths to actual layout)

In `cookimport/bench/suite.py`, define:

```
class BenchItem(BaseModel):
    item_id: str
    source_path: str
    gold_dir: str
    force_source_match: bool = False
    notes: str | None = None

class BenchSuite(BaseModel):
    name: str
    items: list[BenchItem]
```

In `cookimport/bench/pred_run.py`, define an offline-compatible builder:

```
def build_pred_run_for_source(
    source_path: Path,
    out_dir: Path,
    *,
    trace: bool,
    config: dict | None,
) -> Path
    """
    Writes a pred-run folder compatible with freeform eval.
    Must not upload and must not require Label Studio env vars.
    Returns path to pred-run root.
    """
```

In `cookimport/bench/run.py`, define:

```
def run_suite(
    suite: BenchSuite,
    out_dir: Path,
    *,
    config: dict | None,
    trace: bool,
    baseline_run_dir: Path | None,
) -> None
```

This should:

* build or reuse pred-runs,
* invoke existing freeform eval function(s),
* aggregate metrics,
* write `report.md`, `metrics.json`, and `iteration_packet/`.

In `cookimport/bench/packet.py`, define:

```
def build_iteration_packet(run_root: Path) -> None
```

This should read existing eval artifacts (missed/false-positive JSONL, eval_report.json) and augment them with block text context, signals, and (optional) trace excerpts.

In `cookimport/bench/knobs.py` (or reuse existing config system if present), define:

```
class Tunable(BaseModel):
    name: str
    kind: str
    default: object
    bounds: tuple[object, object] | None
    description: str

def load_config(path: Path | None) -> dict
def effective_knobs(config: dict) -> dict
def list_knobs() -> list[Tunable]
```

In `cookimport/bench/sweep.py`, define:

```
def run_sweep(...): ...
```

## Plan revision note

(2026-02-12) Revised the plan to: (1) reference `docs/PLANS.md` correctly, (2) explicitly build on the current freeform export/eval contracts and artifacts, (3) prioritize an explicit non-interactive **offline** benchmark mode (no upload, no LS creds), (4) align output paths under `data/golden/bench/…` to reduce path confusion, and (5) embed known footguns (source mismatch, split-job rebasing, unlabeled≠negative, timestamp/ID drift) with concrete mitigations.

## docs/plans/OGplans/I3.1 Unstructured-based partit.md

```markdown
---
summary: "Archived original ExecPlan for unstructured-first EPUB partitioning strategy."
read_when:
  - When reviewing historical extractor design options
  - When comparing initial partitioning plan to implemented adapter behavior
---

# I3.1 — Purpose / Big Picture: Unstructured-first EPUB block extraction (blocks + roles + traceability)

This ExecPlan is a living document and must be maintained as work progresses, per PLANS.md (repo root).
It is written to be executable by a stateless agent (or a novice human) with only the working tree and this file.

## Purpose / Big Picture

Today, EPUB ingestion produces a linear stream of Blocks that downstream systems treat as the “truth” for:
(1) recipe candidate segmentation (finding recipe boundaries, ingredients, and instructions), and
(2) knowledge extraction (chunking + tip/topic mining from non-recipe content).

When the EPUB “HTML → Blocks” step is noisy or poorly segmented, everything downstream becomes brittle:
recipes get chopped in the wrong places, ingredient/instruction grouping becomes unreliable, and technique chapters become an undifferentiated wall of prose that chunking struggles to lane as “knowledge” vs “noise”.

After this change, EPUB ingestion will produce cleaner, more semantically meaningful Blocks by using Unstructured’s HTML partitioner on each EPUB spine document. Those Blocks will carry explicit traceability metadata (including Unstructured element_id) and a lightweight deterministic “block_role” label. This should improve segmentation stability, improve knowledge chunk lane assignment, and make regressions far easier to diagnose by inspecting a persisted, element-level raw artifact.

What you should be able to do after this is implemented (observable outcomes):

1. Run:

    cookimport stage data/input/<book>.epub --workers 1

   with the Unstructured extractor enabled, and see:
   - the run completes successfully,
   - final drafts show fewer obvious boundary errors on known-problem recipes,
   - technique/intro material yields more “knowledge” chunks (not all “noise”).

2. Inspect the run artifacts and directly answer:
   “What did we extract?” and “Where did this block come from?” without re-running:
   - a new raw artifact file exists containing one JSON object per Unstructured element,
   - each Block retains the originating Unstructured element_id (and stable element_index) so diffs are actionable.

### Scope (explicit)

This ExecPlan standardizes the “all the way through unstructured-source” path for EPUB only:
- We partition EPUB spine HTML/XHTML using Unstructured.
- We DO NOT standardize PDFs (or other formats) in this plan.
  PDF standardization is a follow-up because PDF extraction uses different upstream primitives (page/bbox/OCR lines) and will require a separate adapter and validation strategy.

## Progress

Update this list as you work. Every stopping point must be reflected here.

- [x] (2026-02-12) Expanded ExecPlan to be more self-contained, added traceability requirements (element_id), clarified EPUB-only scope, and added optional Unstructured chunk_by_title milestone.
- [ ] Baseline: pick a representative EPUB with known issues; run legacy extractor with --workers 1 and --workers 2; preserve run roots + reports for later diff.
- [ ] Add Unstructured dependency + disable telemetry defaults for dev/CI; add a clear extractor switch (env var).
- [ ] Implement partition_html_to_blocks adapter (Unstructured Element → Block mapping) INCLUDING capturing Unstructured element_id into Block.features and into diagnostics JSONL.
- [ ] Wire adapter into cookimport/plugins/epub.py in a way that preserves start_spine/end_spine split behavior and global ordering invariants.
- [ ] Emit a new raw artifact: unstructured_elements.jsonl (one row per element, with stable keys suitable for diffing).
- [ ] Implement deterministic block_role enrichment and integrate it into knowledge chunk lane selection (knowledge vs noise).
- [ ] Tests:
  - [ ] Unit tests for Element→Block mapping (types, heading levels, spine_index, element_id capture).
  - [ ] Integration-ish test ensuring split spine ranges merge deterministically (ordering + block index rebasing expectations).
- [ ] Validation: compare before/after report metrics + spot-check known-bad recipes + spot-check chunk lane behavior; record results under Artifacts and Notes.
- [ ] (Optional) Boundary experiment: compare current chunker boundaries vs Unstructured chunk_by_title boundaries on the same non-recipe stream; record findings and decide whether to keep the optional mode.

## Surprises & Discoveries

Record unexpected behaviors with evidence (short snippets, command outputs, paths).

## Decision Log

Record decisions in the format: Decision / Rationale / Date/Author.

- Decision: Partition per EPUB spine document using Unstructured’s HTML partitioner (not unstructured.partition.epub.partition_epub).
  Rationale: Preserves existing start_spine/end_spine splitting and avoids Pandoc/system-level deps; keeps ordering + merge invariants intact.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-12 / plan author

- Decision: Store Unstructured element_id (and a stable derived key) on every Block and in unstructured_elements.jsonl.
  Rationale: Improves traceability and regression diffing; prevents “why did boundaries change?” from becoming guesswork.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-12 / plan author

- Decision: Scope is EPUB-only in this ExecPlan; PDF “standardized blocks via Unstructured” is a follow-up plan.
  Rationale: PDF extraction primitives differ (layout/OCR); bundling would blur acceptance criteria and increase risk.
  Date/Author: 2026-02-12 / plan author
