```markdown
## Context and Orientation

If you are new to this repo, read this section carefully before editing code.

### Glossary (repo-local meanings)

Block:
A low-level ordered text unit used during extraction and segmentation. Blocks are the primary coordinate system for segmentation.
Blocks include text plus a features dictionary that stores extractor metadata (for EPUB, this includes spine_index and will now include Unstructured fields).

RecipeCandidate:
A segmented recipe record (schema-like) produced after segmentation finds a block-range that looks like a recipe and field extraction populates name/ingredients/instructions/etc.

nonRecipeBlocks:
Blocks not covered by any recipe candidate ranges. This is the main input to knowledge chunking later.

KnowledgeChunk:
A coherent non-recipe region built from nonRecipeBlocks; lane-assigned as “knowledge” or “noise” and later mined for tips/topics.

Raw artifact:
A persisted debug output written under the run root’s raw/ directory. For split jobs, workers write raw artifacts under .job_parts/... and the main process merges them into raw/ on success (collisions are resolved by prefixing filenames with the job index).

### Current end-to-end EPUB flow (high level)

When you run:

    cookimport stage data/input/<book>.epub

The concrete flow is:
- registry selects EpubImporter
- EpubImporter.convert() extracts a linear block stream (today via HTML structure)
- blocks are normalized and enriched with signals
- recipe candidate segmentation runs over block indices
- blocks not in recipes are collected as nonRecipeBlocks
- stage pipeline uses nonRecipeBlocks to generate chunks; writers emit drafts/tips/topics/chunks/raw/report

### Output structure you will use during validation

Stage writes a timestamped run root under the output directory (commonly data/output/<timestamp>/...).

Key outputs to inspect:
- final drafts/<workbook_slug>/r{index}.json
- chunks/<workbook_slug>/chunks.md (if chunks exist)
- raw/<importer>/<source_hash>/<location_id>.<ext>
- <workbook_slug>.excel_import_report.json (written at run root)

### Split-job behavior (EPUB)

EPUB stage can split by spine ranges when --workers > 1:
- each worker converts only [start_spine, end_spine)
- Blocks must carry absolute spine_index so merge ordering is deterministic across jobs
- raw artifacts are written to .job_parts/<workbook_slug>/job_<index>/raw/... and merged into raw/ on success

Known limitation to keep in mind:
- EPUB split jobs do not detect recipes that span spine boundaries; a recipe can be split at a spine boundary today.
  This plan does not fix that, but you must ensure the Unstructured integration does not make it worse (and does not break merge).

### Where you will likely edit code

You will almost certainly touch:
- cookimport/plugins/epub.py
  - the spine iteration + HTML-to-Block extraction path
  - the handling of start_spine/end_spine
- cookimport/parsing/
  - new: unstructured_adapter.py (Element→Block mapping)
  - new: block_roles.py (deterministic block_role labeling)
  - existing: signals.py and chunks.py (integration points for roles and heading levels)
- cookimport/staging/ (only if raw artifact writing needs a new helper or naming convention)

## Plan of Work

Milestones are ordered so each is independently verifiable, with minimal blast radius.

### Milestone 0 — Establish a baseline and a “known bad” fixture

Goal:
Lock in “before” behavior so we can prove improvement and catch regressions.

Work:
Pick one representative EPUB that currently exhibits:
- recipe segmentation boundary errors (missing ingredients/instructions, wrong start/end),
- noisy non-recipe extraction (intro/technique chapters that become unusable for chunks).

Run baseline twice (legacy extractor):
- single worker:

    cookimport stage data/input/<book>.epub --workers 1

- split workers:

    cookimport stage data/input/<book>.epub --workers 2

Preserve these artifacts (do not overwrite; copy paths into Artifacts and Notes):
- the run root paths for both runs
- <workbook_slug>.excel_import_report.json
- a small sample of final drafts/<workbook_slug>/r*.json
- chunks/<workbook_slug>/chunks.md (if present)

Acceptance:
You can later diff “legacy vs Unstructured” using saved run roots without re-running the baseline.

### Milestone 1 — Add Unstructured dependency and safe configuration plumbing

Goal:
Introduce Unstructured safely, without silent telemetry surprises, and with a clear rollback switch.

Work:
1) Add the Python dependency (pin to a narrow range to avoid behavior drift).
   Prefer a pin similar to:

    unstructured>=0.18.32,<0.19

   Adjust if the repo already pins unstructured (match repo conventions).

2) Disable telemetry by default for local/dev/CI.
   Document (and use in CI if appropriate):

    DO_NOT_TRACK=true

   If the project uses a .env.example or similar, add it there and mention it in docs.

3) Add an extractor switch.
   Keep the default as legacy until validation is complete.

   Recommended:
   - Env var: C3IMP_EPUB_EXTRACTOR=legacy|unstructured
   - Default: legacy

Failure mode decision (must be explicit in code and documented here):
- Prefer hard-fail when explicitly set to unstructured:
  If C3IMP_EPUB_EXTRACTOR=unstructured and partitioning fails, surface the error loudly rather than silently falling back.
  (Silent fallback hides regressions and makes debugging ambiguous.)
- If you choose fallback anyway, record the rationale in Decision Log and ensure the logs make it unmistakable.

Footgun to anticipate:
Unstructured (or a dependency) may try to download NLP resources the first time it runs (environment-dependent).
If you encounter a “missing punkt” / NLTK-data style error:
- decide whether to vendor required data in-repo (preferred for deterministic CI) or
- document an explicit one-time setup step and ensure CI has network access (less preferred).
Record what you did in Surprises & Discoveries.

Acceptance:
- The repo installs and imports unstructured reliably in dev and CI contexts.
- A single switch controls the EPUB extractor behavior.

### Milestone 2 — Implement the Unstructured adapter: HTML → Blocks (with traceability)

Goal:
Build a small, testable mapping layer that converts Unstructured elements into the repo’s Block model while preserving ordering, split-job invariants, and traceability.

Key requirement added in this revision:
Capture Unstructured element_id explicitly and propagate it:
- into Block.features (per Block), and
- into the JSONL diagnostics artifact, so regressions are easy to diff.

Work:
Create a new module:

- cookimport/parsing/unstructured_adapter.py

Define a single, testable entrypoint:

    partition_html_to_blocks(
        html: str,
        *,
        spine_index: int,
        source_location_id: str,
    ) -> tuple[list[Block], list[dict]]

Returns:
- blocks: list of Block objects in stable extracted order (element order within a spine doc)
- diagnostics_rows: JSON-serializable dicts, one per element, suitable for JSONL persistence

Mapping rules (first pass; keep deterministic and easy to reason about):
1) Element filtering:
- Skip elements whose text is empty or whitespace-only after normalization.

2) Type mapping:
Map Unstructured element category to Block.type using a simple table:
- Title -> heading
- NarrativeText -> paragraph
- ListItem -> list_item
- Table -> table
- other/unknown -> paragraph (or other if the codebase has an “other” type)

3) Features and traceability (IMPORTANT):
In Block.features, include (at minimum):
- spine_index (absolute)
- source_location_id (so provenance can correlate)
- unstructured_category (string category name)
- unstructured_category_depth (int, default 0)
- unstructured_parent_id (string or null, if available)
- unstructured_element_id (string or null, if available)   <-- REQUIRED BY USER
- unstructured_element_index (int)                          <-- REQUIRED FOR STABLE DIFFS
- unstructured_stable_key (string)                          <-- RECOMMENDED

Rationale for stable_key:
Unstructured element_id may not be stable across versions/runs; a stable_key derived from coordinates is diff-friendly.
Recommended definition:

- unstructured_stable_key = f"{source_location_id}:spine{spine_index}:e{element_index}"

4) Heading levels:
If the element is a Title, derive a heading level using category depth as a proxy:

- heading_level = clamp(unstructured_category_depth + 1, 1, 6)

Store it where the repo expects (often Block.features["heading_level"] or a dedicated field if Block has one).

5) Text normalization:
Be careful not to “double-normalize” in a way that changes semantics.
If the repo already runs a shared cleaning pipeline (NFKC, whitespace standardization, etc.), align with that:
- either apply the same cleaning to element text here, or
- keep raw text here and rely on downstream normalization (preferred if that is already guaranteed).
Whichever you choose, document it in Decision Log.

6) Ordering invariants:
- Preserve Unstructured’s returned order within each spine document.
- Preserve spine document order by iterating spine_index ascending.
- Do not sort elements by text or category; ordering is part of the coordinate system used by segmentation.

Diagnostics rows (for JSONL):
For each element, emit a dict with:
- source_location_id
- spine_index
- element_index
- element_id (unstructured_element_id)
- stable_key (unstructured_stable_key)
- category, category_depth, parent_id
- text (full text; if size becomes an issue, add text_hash and optionally truncate text but keep hash)
- any other cheap metadata that helps debugging (e.g., html_tag if available)

Acceptance:
- The adapter can convert a small HTML snippet into Blocks and diagnostics deterministically.
- Each Block produced from Unstructured carries unstructured_element_id (when available) and always carries unstructured_element_index + stable_key.

### Milestone 3 — Wire the adapter into the EPUB importer (preserve split behavior)

Goal:
Enable Unstructured-based extraction for EPUBs without breaking:
- start_spine/end_spine slicing
- global ordering across slices
- merge correctness and downstream block index coordinate space

Work:
In cookimport/plugins/epub.py:
1) Identify the existing spine iteration loop and the function(s) that currently convert spine HTML/XHTML into Blocks.

2) Add an alternate extraction path selected by C3IMP_EPUB_EXTRACTOR:
- For each spine doc in the worker’s assigned [start_spine, end_spine):
  - obtain html string using existing EPUB extraction logic
  - call partition_html_to_blocks(html, spine_index=..., source_location_id=...)
  - accumulate returned blocks in a list (job-local)
  - accumulate diagnostics rows (job-local)

3) Ensure each Block has absolute spine_index in its features.
Downstream merge and ordering depend on it.

4) Ensure existing raw artifact “full_text” behavior is preserved.
If the EPUB importer currently writes extracted blocks JSON as full_text, keep doing that (legacy and unstructured should both produce comparable artifacts).

Acceptance:
- Running cookimport stage on a small EPUB with the switch enabled produces a coherent Block stream and does not crash.
- Split job conversion still runs for a spine range and emits consistent outputs.

### Milestone 4 — Persist Unstructured diagnostics as a raw artifact (jsonl)

Goal:
Make extraction debuggable without re-running with ad-hoc logging, and make regressions easy to diff.

Work:
1) Write a new raw artifact file containing diagnostics rows:

- name: unstructured_elements.jsonl
- format: one JSON object per line (no surrounding array)

2) Use the existing raw artifact mechanism so it lands under the standard raw path:
- raw/epub/<source_hash>/<location_id>.<ext>
(Exact naming conventions may vary; keep consistent with existing artifact writer behavior.)

3) Split-job handling:
- Each worker writes its own diagnostics file under .job_parts/<workbook_slug>/job_<index>/raw/...
- The main process merges/moves raw artifacts into raw/ on success.
- Name collisions are resolved by prefixing filenames with job index; do not rely on collisions as a strategy.

4) Include minimal mapping metadata somewhere:
Either:
- include a small header row at the top of the JSONL (not ideal for JSONL tooling), or
- write a companion sidecar file (recommended), e.g.:
  - unstructured_elements.meta.json
    containing unstructured version, extractor switch value, and mapping table.

Acceptance:
- After a successful run, unstructured_elements.jsonl exists under raw/ for EPUB runs when Unstructured is enabled.
- For --workers > 1, the artifact exists after merge and .job_parts is cleaned on success (and preserved on failure for debugging).

### Milestone 5 — Add deterministic block_role enrichment and integrate into chunk lane assignment

Goal:
Improve knowledge extraction by avoiding the “everything narrative becomes noise” failure mode, without introducing non-deterministic ML.

Work:
Create a module:

- cookimport/parsing/block_roles.py

Define:

    assign_block_roles(blocks: list[Block]) -> None

Rules should be:
- deterministic
- cheap
- explainable (easy to debug)
- aligned with Label Studio canonical/freeform vocabulary where possible

Recommended first-pass roles (stored as Block.features["block_role"]):
- recipe_title
- ingredient_line
- instruction_line
- tip_like
- narrative_science
- narrative_fluff
- other

Heuristic suggestions (keep conservative to avoid false positives):
- If block is heading and matches recipe title cues -> recipe_title
- If signals indicate ingredient-like (starts_with_quantity, has_unit, ingredient_
```

## docs/plans/OGplans/I4.1 Auto-tag recipes with a catalog-dri.md

```markdown
---
summary: "Archived original ExecPlan for catalog-driven recipe auto-tagging."
read_when:
  - When reviewing historical tagging architecture and rollout decisions
  - When reconciling old plan details with current tagging implementation
---

# Auto-tag recipes with a catalog-driven rule engine (LLM-ready)

This ExecPlan is a living document. The sections `Progress`, `Surprises & Discoveries`, `Decision Log`, and `Outcomes & Retrospective` must be kept up to date as work proceeds.

This plan must be maintained in accordance with `PLANS.md` at the repository root.


## Purpose / Big Picture

After this change, a user can run a single CLI command to automatically suggest (and optionally apply) recipe tags from the existing tag catalog, without hard-coding tag IDs. The system will:

1) Load the current tag catalog at runtime (so adding tags later is naturally supported).

2) Run a deterministic, rule-based tagger first (regex + lightweight parsing over recipe title/notes/ingredients/steps + a few numeric fields like total time).

3) Optionally call an LLM as a “second pass” only for the categories the deterministic tagger cannot confidently fill, using a short-listed candidate set so the prompt stays small.

The observable outcome is that you can point the tool at staged recipe drafts (`data/output/.../final drafts/.../*.json`) or at recipe rows in Postgres/Supabase, and get a clear list of tags with confidence and “why” evidence. If `--apply` is used, the tool will insert rows into `public.recipe_tag_assignments` safely and idempotently (re-running does not create duplicates).

How to see it working (end state):

    # 1) Export catalog once (or load directly from DB every time)
    cookimport tag-catalog export --db-url "$COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL" --out data/tagging/tag_catalog.json

    # 2) Suggest tags for staged drafts (dry run)
    cookimport tag-recipes suggest --draft-dir "data/output/<run>/final drafts/<workbook>/" \
      --catalog-json data/tagging/tag_catalog.json \
      --out-dir "data/output/<run>/tags/<workbook>/" \
      --explain

    # 3) Suggest + apply tags for one DB recipe (optional)
    cookimport tag-recipes apply --db-url "$COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL" --recipe-id "<uuid>" \
      --catalog-json data/tagging/tag_catalog.json \
      --explain


## Scope / Guardrails (avoid accidental damage)

- This plan is about **auto-suggesting** tags from the existing catalog and optionally writing **assignments**. It does **not** create new tags/categories or change the catalog schema.
- DB writes are **insert-only** (`ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`). We will not delete/replace tags in this plan because the schema does not track “who assigned this tag,” and deletion risks removing user curation.
- Precision-first: prefer missing a tag over adding a wrong tag. Start conservative and expand coverage iteratively.
- LLM support is optional, disabled by default, and must fail safe (no provider configured ⇒ deterministic only).

## Quality Bar (explicit)

Before enabling DB apply on any meaningful batch:

- Determinism: same inputs + same catalog ⇒ identical outputs (ordering, confidence, evidence).
- Evidence: every suggested tag includes at least one human-readable reason (field + matched phrase where possible).
- Conservative defaults: especially for “single” categories (main protein/carb, course, meal type, etc.).
- A small gold set exists (even 20–50 recipes) with an eval harness to prevent regressions while rules evolve.


## Progress

- [ ] (2026-02-12) Read existing CLI structure (`cookimport/cli.py`) and add a new Typer command group for tagging (`tag-catalog`, `tag-recipes`).
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Implement tag catalog loader + exporter (DB → `tag_catalog.json`) and prove it reports expected counts.
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Add a tiny gold set + eval harness so rule iterations don’t regress precision.
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Implement `RecipeSignalPack` extraction from (a) staged cookbook3 drafts and (b) DB rows (recipes + steps + ingredient lines).
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Implement deterministic tagging engine (rules keyed by `recipe_tags.key_norm`) with per-category constraints and human-readable evidence.
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Implement CLI flows: `suggest` for drafts and `apply` for DB (idempotent inserts, `--dry-run`, `--explain`, writes a run report).
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Add catalog fingerprinting + drift checks so DB apply cannot silently write wrong tag IDs.
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Add unit tests for rule scoring + category policy behavior; add a small end-to-end test over fixture drafts.
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Add (stubbed) LLM second-pass interface behind a flag; default off; include a mocked implementation that keeps tests deterministic.
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Document usage in repo docs/help text and include a “how to add rules” note for extending deterministic coverage.


## Surprises & Discoveries

None yet. As you implement, record any schema mismatches, unexpected draft field names, or performance bottlenecks here with short evidence (query output, stack traces, etc.).


## Decision Log

- Decision (2026-02-12): The tagger will be catalog-driven at runtime: it will resolve `key_norm -> id` by reading the catalog, and rules will be keyed by `key_norm` (never by numeric/UUID IDs). This makes “adding 3 new tags tomorrow” fit naturally: the catalog changes are picked up without code changes.
- Decision (2026-02-12): Deterministic tagging happens first, and the LLM is a gated second pass that only runs for “missing/low-confidence categories,” to reduce cost and keep behavior stable.
- Decision (2026-02-12): DB writes are insert-only with `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` against the `(recipe_id, tag_id)` primary key. We will not delete/replace tags in this plan because the schema does not track “who assigned this tag,” and deletion risks removing user curation.


## Outcomes & Retrospective

Pending. When complete, summarize what was shipped, how accurate it is on a small sample set, and what the next most valuable incremental improvements are.


## Context and Orientation

This repository is a Python 3.12 ingestion and normalization pipeline with a Typer CLI (`cookimport`). A common workflow is `cookimport stage <path>`, which produces intermediate drafts and final cookbook3 drafts on disk under `data/output/<timestamp>/...`, including:

- `intermediate drafts/<workbook>/r{index}.jsonld`
- `final drafts/<workbook>/r{index}.json`

The transformation to final cookbook3 drafts happens in `write_draft_outputs(...)` via `recipe_candidate_to_draft_v1(...)`, where ingredient parsing and step linking run uniformly across sources.

Separately, the product database schema stores recipes and tagging using these tables:

- `public.recipes` for recipe-level fields (title, description, times, etc.)
- `public.recipe_steps` for ordered instructions
- `public.step_ingredient_lines` for ingredient lines (raw text + parsed numeric/unit fields)
- `public.recipe_tags` is the tag catalog (`id`, `key_norm`, `display_name`, `category_id`, ...)
- `public.recipe_tag_assignments` stores assignments (PK is `(recipe_id, tag_id)`)

The tag catalog is seeded (and should remain the source of truth for initial tags) via `supabase/seeds/catalog.sql`. The current catalog is “20 categories” and “203 recipe tags.”

This ExecPlan adds a new “tagging” subsystem to `cookimport` that can operate on staged drafts (files) and optionally on database rows (Postgres/Supabase).


## Definitions (avoid jargon)

- Tag catalog: The set of allowed tags and their metadata. In this repo, it’s the rows of `public.recipe_tags` plus the category table those tags reference.
- Tag key_norm: A stable, normalized string key for a tag (example style: `instant-pot`, `weeknight`). We key rules and I/O off this value.
- Category: A grouping of tags (“cooking-style”, “main-protein”, etc.) that may have constraints such as “pick at most one tag in this category.”
- Deterministic tagger: A rule engine that assigns tags based on explicit string/regex matches and simple numeric heuristics, producing repeatable outputs.
- LLM second pass: An optional step that chooses tags when deterministic rules are uncertain, using the existing catalog as the allowed label set.
- Evidence: A short explanation of why a tag was suggested (for example: “matched ‘instant pot’ in title”).


## Architecture Overview

We will build a small, testable tagging library plus CLI plumbing:

1) Catalog loading:
   - Load categories + tags from the database (preferred) or from an exported JSON snapshot file.
   - Build lookups: by `key_norm`, by `category_key_norm`, by `category_id`.

2) Signal extraction:
   - Convert a recipe (draft file or DB rows) into a `RecipeSignalPack`:
     - normalized text fields: title, description, notes
     - lists of ingredient strings and instruction strings
     - numeric metadata: total_time_minutes, prep_time_minutes, cook_time_minutes, yield phrase, etc.

3) Deterministic scoring:
   - For a curated subset of tags (starting with high-signal categories like cooking style, equipment, effort, main protein/carb, cooking method), compute a confidence score from 0..1 and attach evidence.
   - Apply category policies:
     - “single”: pick only the top tag if above threshold
     - “multi”: pick all tags above threshold, up to a max

4) Optional LLM second pass:
   - Only for categories that are required or important but missing/low-confidence after deterministic scoring.
   - Provide a short list of candidate tags per category (generated via fuzzy matching over tag display names) instead of dumping all 203 tags into the prompt.


## Milestone 0: Eval harness + tiny gold set (recommended)

Why:

Rules will evolve quickly. Without a small evaluation harness, you will drift into silent false positives (especially in “single” categories). A tiny gold set gives you a safety net while iterating.

Scope:

At the end of this milestone, there is a small, fast test suite that measures tag suggestion correctness on a tiny labeled dataset, and fails CI on obvious regressions.

Work:

1) Add `tests/tagging_gold/` (or similar):

- A small fixture catalog, e.g. `tag_catalog.small.json` (subset of categories/tags used in tests).
- 20–50 fixture recipes (either cookbook3 drafts or minimal `RecipeSignalPack` JSON).
- Gold labels mapping `fixture_id -> expected tag_key_norms`.

2) Add an eval helper (`cookimport/tagging/eval.py`):

- Compute at least precision/recall per category (or at minimum: protected-category precision).
- Keep thresholds conservative; start by protecting “single” categories from false positives.

3) Wire into tests:

- `pytest -q` should run quickly and fail loudly on regressions.

Acceptance:

    pytest -q

Should be fast and deterministic, and should catch when a rule change introduces a new wrong tag for a protected category.


## Milestone 1: Add tag catalog models + loader/exporter (DB → JSON)

Scope:

At the end of this milestone, we can load the full tag catalog and export it to a JSON file, and we can verify the catalog size (category count and tag count) matches expectations.

Work:

1) Create a new package directory:

- `cookimport/tagging/`
  - `__init__.py`
  - `catalog.py`
  - `catalog_export.py` (optional, if you want exporter helpers separate)

2) In `cookimport/tagging/catalog.py`, implement these models and lookups:

- `TagCategory` (id, key_norm, display_name, sort_order)
- `Tag` (id, key_norm, display_name, category_id, sort_order)
- `TagCatalog`
  - `categories_by_id: dict[uuid, TagCategory]`
  - `categories_by_key: dict[str, TagCategory]`
  - `tags_by_id: dict[uuid, Tag]`
  - `tags_by_key: dict[str, Tag]`
  - `tags_by_category_id: dict[uuid, list[Tag]]`
  - helper methods:
    - `get_tag_id(key_norm: str) -> uuid | None`
    - `get_category_key(category_id: uuid) -> str | None`

3) Implement catalog loading:

- `load_catalog_from_db(db_url: str) -> TagCatalog`
  - Use `psycopg` (Postgres driver) for a direct SQL query.
  - Add dependency to `pyproject.toml` (or requirements) as needed: `psycopg[binary]`.

  Queries to implement (confirm exact category table name in `db/schema.snapshot.sql` and/or `supabase/seeds/catalog.sql` first):

    - Categories:
        SELECT id, key_norm, display_name, sort_order
        FROM public.<CATEGORY_TABLE>;

    - Tags:
        SELECT id, key_norm, display_name, category_id, sort_order
        FROM public.recipe_tags;

  Important: If the category table name is not obvious, locate it by searching `db/schema.snapshot.sql` for `recipe_tags` foreign keys or for `key_norm` in tag-category inserts. Record the final table name in the Decision Log.

- `load_catalog_from_json(path: Path) -> TagCatalog`
- `export_catalog_to_json(catalog: TagCatalog, path: Path) -> None`
  - Include `exported_at`, counts, and a `catalog_fingerprint` (sha256 over a deterministic payload) so tagging runs and DB apply can detect catalog drift.

4) Add a new CLI command:

- In `cookimport/cli.py`, add a Typer group:

    @app.command("tag-catalog")
    ...

  Recommended subcommand layout:

- `cookimport tag-catalog export --db-url ... --out ...`
  - Default `--db-url` to env var `COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL`.

Acceptance:

From repo root, run:

    cookimport tag-catalog export --db-url "$COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL" --out data/tagging/tag_catalog.json

Expected output should include:

- “Loaded N categories, M tags”
- N should be 20 and M should be 203 in the default seed state.
- `data/tagging/tag_catalog.json` should exist and contain both categories and tags.
- The JSON should include a `catalog_fingerprint` (and counts) so downstream commands can record exactly what catalog version was used.

If DB is not available in your environment, allow a fallback acceptance path:

- Add `cookimport tag-catalog export --from-seed supabase/seeds/catalog.sql --out ...` as a “best effort” parser that only extracts `key_norm` + display names (even if category IDs are not stable).
- This fallback is optional; do not block DB mode on it if it becomes complex. If you implement it, keep it clearly labeled as a fallback and add tests for it.


## Milestone 2: Implement RecipeSignalPack extraction (drafts + DB)

Scope:

At the end of this milestone, we can take either:
- a cookbook3 draft JSON file from `final drafts/`, or
- a DB recipe id

…and produce a `RecipeSignalPack` with normalized text and numeric metadata.

Work:

1) Create `cookimport/tagging/signals.py` with:

- `RecipeSignalPack`
  - `recipe_id: str | None` (uuid string for DB mode; None for pure draft files)
  - `title: str`
  - `description: str`
  - `notes: str`
  - `ingredients: list[str]`
  - `instructions: list[str]`
  - `prep_time_minutes: int | None`
  - `cook_time_minutes: int | None`
  - `total_time_minutes: int | None`
  - `yield_phrase: str | None`
  - `max_oven_temp_f: int | None`
  - `spice_level: int | None`
  - `attention_level: str | None`
  - `cleanup_level: str | None`

2) Add a small normalization helper:

- `normalize_text_for_matching(s: str) -> str`
  - lower-case
  - strip accents (unicode normalize)
  - replace punctuation with spaces
  - collapse repeated whitespace

3) Draft signal extraction:

- `signals_from_draft_json(path: Path) -> RecipeSignalPack`
  - Load JSON.
  - Parse to the repository’s cookbook3 model if available (search for `RecipeDraftV1` in `cookimport/core/models.py`), but do not block if the draft format differs. If model parse fails, fall back to dictionary access and log a short warning.
  - Extract:
    - title/description/notes
    - ingredient lines: ideally from the already-parsed ingredient line structures if present; otherwise from raw ingredient text arrays
    - instructions: from recipe steps (ordered)
    - numeric fields: times/yield if present

4) DB signal extraction:

- Create `cookimport/tagging/db_read.py` (or put in `signals.py` if small) that fetches:

  - `public.recipes` (title/description/notes/times/yield/levels fields)
  - `public.recipe_steps` (ordered; include `instruction_text`)
  - `public.step_ingredient_lines` (ordered; include `raw_text`, optionally parsed fields)

- Provide:

  - `fetch_recipe_bundle(db_url: str, recipe_id: uuid) -> RecipeSignalPack`

5) Add a debug CLI:

- `cookimport tag-recipes debug-signals --draft <path>`
- `cookimport tag-recipes debug-signals --db-url ... --recipe-id ...`

Acceptance:

- Running debug-signals prints:
  - title, and counts (# ingredient lines, # instructions)
  - the numeric fields (times, yield) if present
- Both draft mode and DB mode produce a `RecipeSignalPack` that can be passed into the tagger (next milestone).


## Milestone 3: Deterministic tagging engine (rules + category policies)

Scope:

At the end of this milestone, we can run deterministic tagging for a recipe and get a list of suggested tag `key_norm` values with confidence and evidence, and we can enforce simple “single vs multi” category rules.

Work:

1) Create `cookimport/tagging/rules.py` containing a pure-Python ruleset keyed by tag `key_norm`.

Rule format (keep it intentionally simple and editable):

- `TAG_RULES: dict[str, dict]` where each entry can contain:

  - `patterns`: list of pattern rules:
    - `field`: one of `title`, `description`, `notes`, `ingredients`, `instructions`
    - `regex`: a python regex string (assume normalized text)
    - `weight`: float (typical 0.2–1.0)
    - `evidence`: short text template for “why”
  - `exclude_patterns` (optional): list of regex strings; if any match, suppress this tag (prevents common false positives).
  - `min_score`: float threshold for this tag (default 0.6)

Example (do not use code fences inside this ExecPlan; this is shown as an indented shape only):

    TAG_RULES = {
      "instant-pot": {
        "min_score": 0.7,
        "patterns": [
          {"field": "title", "regex": r"\binstant pot\b|\bip\b", "weight": 0.8, "evidence": "matched Instant Pot in title"},
          {"field": "instructions", "regex": r"\bpressure cook\b|\bnatural release\b|\bquick release\b", "weight": 0.4, "evidence": "matched pressure-cooker phrasing in instructions"},
        ],
      },
      "slow-cooker": {
        "min_score": 0.7,
        "patterns": [
          {"field": "title", "regex": r"\bslow cooker\b|\bcrock[- ]pot\b", "weight": 0.8, "evidence": "matched slow cooker in title"},
        ],
      },
      ...
    }

Rule authoring footguns (read before adding patterns):

- Prefer ingredient-driven signals for main protein/carb; title-only matches are a common source of false positives.
- Beware short ambiguous tokens (e.g., `ip`). If you include them, require a second supporting match (instructions phrasing) or add exclude patterns for common collisions.
- Always use word boundaries in regex where appropriate; normalization can change punctuation/spacing and create accidental matches.
- Add at least one negative test when you add a new high-impact rule.

Start with a curated subset that delivers value quickly and is relatively low-risk:

- Cooking Style / Equipment / Cooking Method:
  - instant-pot, slow-cooker, air-fryer, grill, sheet-pan, one-pot, no-cook, stovetop-only, oven-only
  - blender, food-processor, dutch-oven, wok, cast-iron (equipment category)
  - bake/roast/grill/steam/simmer/saute (cooking-method category)

- Effort:
  - quick (total_time_minutes <= 25 or title contains “quick”)
  - hands-off-friendly (attention_level == set_and_forget OR “simmer for 2 hours” signals; keep conservative)
  - minimal-prep / minimal-chopping (only if clear phrases like “no chopping” / “pre-chopped” appear; otherwise skip)

- Main protein / main carb (ingredient-driven):
  - chicken/beef/pork/fish/shrimp/tofu/chickpeas/lentils/eggs
  - rice/pasta/potatoes/tortillas/bread
  - Keep these conservative: require ingredient matches, not just title mentions.

2) Category policies:

Create `cookimport/tagging/policies.py`:

- `CATEGORY_POLICIES: dict[str, dict]` keyed by category `key_norm`:

  - `mode`: `"single"` or `"multi"`
  - `min_confidence`: default threshold if tag-specific min not provided
  - `max_tags`: for multi categories

Suggested defaults:

- single:
  - `main-protein`, `main-carb`, `meal-type`, `course`
- multi:
  - `equipment`, `cooking-method`, `storage`, `occasion` (but deterministic may not cover all yet; policy still applies when it does)
- leave many categories to LLM later (`cuisine`, `dietary`, `flavor-profile`) by not writing deterministic rules for them yet.

3) Scoring engine:

Create `cookimport/tagging/engine.py`:

- `TagSuggestion`
  - `tag_key: str`
  - `category_key: str`
  - `confidence: float`
  - `evidence: list[str]`

- `suggest_tags_deterministic(catalog: TagCatalog, signals: RecipeSignalPack) -> list[TagSuggestion]`

Algorithm:

- Build normalized searchable strings:
  - title/description/notes: normalized text
  - ingredients/instructions: normalized text joined with newlines (and also keep per-line list for better evidence)
- For each tag in `TAG_RULES`:
  - If tag key is not present in `catalog.tags_by_key`, skip it (this is what makes the ruleset forward-compatible with catalog changes).
  - If any `exclude_patterns` match (in any relevant field), suppress this tag entirely.
  - Compute `raw_score = sum(weight for each matched pattern)`.
  - Convert to `confidence` by clamping: `confidence = min(1.0, max(0.0, raw_score))`.
  - Keep evidence for each matched pattern.
  - Keep the suggestion only if `confidence >= max(rule.min_score, category_policy.min_confidence)`.

- Apply category policies:
  - Group by `category_key`.
  - If mode=single: keep only the highest-confidence tag; if tie, prefer the tag whose `display_name` appears in the title; else stable sort by tag sort_order.
  - If mode=multi: keep up to `max_tags` sorted by confidence descending.

4) Output formatting:

Create `cookimport/tagging/render.py` with:

- `render_suggestions_text(...)` for console (Rich-friendly)
- `serialize_suggestions_json(...)` for writing `*.tags.json` per recipe

Acceptance:

Add a minimal test fixture recipe signal pack and prove deterministic tags work:

    pytest -q

And prove CLI can run deterministic tagger (draft file mode):

    cookimport tag-recipes suggest --draft "data/output/<run>/final drafts/<workbook>/r0.json" \
      --catalog-json data/tagging/tag_catalog.json \
      --explain

Expected output shape (example):

    Recipe: Instant Pot Chicken Chili
    Suggested tags:
      - cooking-style/instant-pot (0.80)  matched Instant Pot in title
      - main-protein/chicken (0.70)       matched 'chicken' in ingredient lines
      - cooking-method/pressure-cook (0.60) matched pressure cook phrasing in instructions

Exact tags will vary based on the fixture content, but the key acceptance criterion is: deterministic + evidence + category policy filtering works.


## Milestone 4: CLI for staged drafts (bulk) + tag output artifacts

Scope:

At the end of this milestone, you can tag an entire staged workbook folder and get `*.tags.json` output files and a run summary report.

Work:

1) Extend `cookimport/cli.py` with a Typer group:

- `cookimport tag-recipes ...`

Add subcommands:

- `cookimport tag-recipes suggest`
  - inputs:
    - `--draft` for one file
    - `--draft-dir` for a folder (recursively find `*.json`)
  - catalog inputs:
    - `--catalog-json PATH` (required for this subcommand; keep DB access in `tag-catalog export`)
  - output:
    - `--out-dir PATH` (optional; if set, write `r{index}.tags.json` files)
    - always write a run report JSON (default: `data/output/<timestamp>/tagging_report.json` unless `--out-dir` implies another location)
  - debug:
    - `--explain` prints evidence
    - `--limit N` for quick iteration

2) Implement “bulk folder” behavior:

- For each draft JSON, call:
  - `signals_from_draft_json(...)`
  - `suggest_tags_deterministic(...)`
  - write `*.tags.json` if requested

- Aggregate summary:
  - total recipes processed
  - average tags per recipe
  - per-category tag counts
  - list of recipes with zero tags (useful to decide where LLM will help later)

Acceptance:

Run:

    cookimport tag-recipes suggest \
      --draft-dir "data/output/<run>/final drafts/<workbook>/" \
      --catalog-json data/tagging/tag_catalog.json \
      --out-dir "data/output/<run>/tags/<workbook>/" \
      --limit 25

Verify:

- Output directory contains `*.tags.json` files.
- The run report JSON exists and includes per-category counts.
- Re-running the same command overwrites the same output files deterministically (same content, same tag ordering).


## Milestone 5: DB apply/backfill (idempotent inserts into recipe_tag_assignments)

Scope:

At the end of this milestone, you can tag a recipe in the database by ID and apply the assignments safely (no duplicates on rerun). You can also backfill a limited batch.

Work:

1) Add `cookimport/tagging/db_write.py`:

- `insert_tag_assignments(db_url: str, recipe_id: uuid, tag_ids: list[uuid]) -> int`
  - Use a transaction.
  - Insert:

        INSERT INTO public.recipe_tag_assignments (recipe_id, tag_id, created_at)
        VALUES (%s, %s, now())
        ON CONFLICT (recipe_id, tag_id) DO NOTHING;

  - Return number of rows inserted.

2) Add CLI subcommand:

- `cookimport tag-recipes apply`
  - inputs:
    - `--db-url` (or env `COOKIMPORT_DATABASE_URL`)
    - `--recipe-id <uuid>` (required for MVP)
  - catalog:
    - `--catalog-json` (recommended)
      - Record `catalog_fingerprint` in the run report.
      - Before writing, verify that every selected `tag_id` exists in the target DB; abort with a clear message if not (catalog drift footgun).
    - (optional) `--catalog-from-db` to force loading catalog from the same DB you will write to.
  - behavior:
    - deterministic suggestions
    - show summary
    - default is dry-run
    - if `--apply` is set, require an explicit confirmation gate (`--yes` or interactive prompt) before writing
    - support `--min-confidence` override

3) Add a limited “batch mode”:

- Optional (but recommended): allow `--import-batch-id <uuid>` or `--source <string>` and `--limit N`.
- The `public.recipes` table has `import_batch_id` and `source`. Use them for safe scoping.

Suggested batch query:

    SELECT id
    FROM public.recipes
    WHERE archived_at IS NULL
      AND (import_batch_id = %s OR %s IS NULL)
      AND (source = %s OR %s IS NULL)
    ORDER BY created_at DESC
    LIMIT %s;

4) Ensure safety and retry:

- All DB writes must be inside a transaction.
- Insert-only and idempotent is required.

Acceptance:

- Apply on one recipe:
  - First run inserts rows.
  - Second run inserts 0 rows (idempotent).
- Batch mode (if implemented) can run with `--dry-run` to preview counts and does not crash when encountering a recipe with missing fields.


## Milestone 6: LLM second pass scaffolding (disabled by default)

Scope:

At the end of this milestone, the CLI can run with `--llm` enabled, but it remains safe and testable even when no real provider key is configured. The LLM call is only made for categories the deterministic engine did not fill confidently.

Work:

1) Add `cookimport/tagging/llm_second_pass.py` that exposes one function:

- `suggest_tags_with_llm(signals: RecipeSignalPack, catalog: TagCatalog, missing_categories: list[str], deterministic: list[TagSuggestion]) -> list[TagSuggestion]`

2) Prompt-injection and safety note:

- Treat recipe text as untrusted input. Instruct the model to output only from provided candidates, and still validate outputs strictly.

3) Candidate shortlisting (important for prompt size):

- For each missing category:
  - Build a shortlist of up to 10 candidate tags by fuzzy matching tag display_name against the recipe’s combined text.
  - You can reuse RapidFuzz (already used in repo) if available; otherwise implement a simple token overlap scorer.

4) LLM interface:

- Use the existing `cookimport/llm/` integration layer. If it is still mocked, implement a mock provider path that returns an empty list, but preserves the end-to-end call shape.
- Define a strict JSON schema for the LLM response, for example:

    {
      "suggestions": [
        {"category": "cuisine", "tag_key": "mexican", "confidence": 0.72, "why": "mentions tortillas + salsa + cumin"},
        ...
      ]
    }

5) Parse and validate (required):

- `tag_key` must exist in catalog.
- `category` must match the tag’s category.
- `confidence` must be 0..1.
- For now, require that `tag_key` is within the candidate shortlist for that category (this keeps prompts small and prevents the model from “inventing” tags).
- Reject (or ignore) any extra keys, free-form text, or schema violations.

6) Fail-safe behavior (required):

- If no provider is configured, warn once and return an empty list (deterministic only).
- If the provider errors or times out, warn and return an empty list.

7) CLI wiring:

- Add `--llm` flag to `cookimport tag-recipes suggest` and `apply`.
- Only call LLM if:
  - flag enabled AND provider configured AND there are missing categories
- Merge deterministic + LLM suggestions and re-apply category policies.

Acceptance:

- With `--llm` on but no provider configured, the CLI should print a single warning and continue with deterministic results.
- With mocked provider, a unit test should prove the code path executes and merges results without crashing.


## Testing Strategy (do not skip)

Add tests under `tests/`:

0) Gold set regression tests:
- The tiny gold set from Milestone 0 must run in CI and protect precision in high-impact categories.

1) Unit tests (fast, deterministic):
- Scoring: given a `RecipeSignalPack`, verify tag confidence and evidence for a small ruleset.
- Category policy: verify “single” keeps only the top tag and “multi” keeps multiple.
- Catalog resolution: verify missing tags in rules are skipped cleanly.

2) End-to-end test (file mode):
- Add a tiny fixture cookbook3 draft JSON under `tests/fixtures/`.
- Add a tiny fixture `tag_catalog.json` subset (just enough tags/categories for the fixture).
- Run `cookimport tag-recipes suggest` in a test and assert output JSON contains expected tag keys.

3) DB integration tests:
- Optional in this plan (depends on CI environment). If CI can run Postgres, add one integration test; otherwise keep DB code covered by unit tests + manual acceptance checks.


## Operational Notes (idempotence, safety, debugging)

- Idempotence:
  - File outputs should be overwritten deterministically.
  - DB inserts must use `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`.

- Debugging:
  - Always support `--explain` to show evidence.
  - Add `cookimport tag-recipes debug-signals` to inspect what the tagger “sees.”

- Catalog drift:
  - If applying tags to DB using a JSON snapshot, verify IDs exist in the target DB before writing.
  - Record `catalog_fingerprint` in every run report.

- Over-tagging:
  - Keep “single” category thresholds conservative; missing is better than wrong.
  - Prefer ingredient-driven evidence for main protein/carb.

- LLM safety:
  - Validate model outputs strictly; ignore anything outside candidates or wrong-category.

- Reporting:
  - Write a run report JSON that records:
    - catalog version info (counts, maybe a hash of `tag_catalog.json`)
    - inputs processed
    - per-recipe selected tags and confidences
    - failures with stack traces (shortened)

- Performance:
  - Keep per-recipe tagging O(number_of_rules) with precompiled regex where possible.
  - For bulk runs, load catalog once and reuse.


## You can do this later: “making new tags” (do not implement now)

This plan intentionally does not implement migrations/UX for creating new tags. The system is designed so new tags fit naturally:

- Add tags/categories to seed + DB.
- Re-export catalog JSON (or load from DB).
- Optionally add deterministic rules keyed by new tag `key_norm`.
- If no rules, LLM second pass (when enabled) can start using the new tag immediately.
- Evaluate and tune thresholds/rules based on false positives/negatives.
```

## docs/plans/OGplans/I5.1 golden set freeform.md

```markdown
---
summary: "Archived original ExecPlan for freeform-span golden-set workflow design."
read_when:
  - When reviewing historical golden-set campaign decisions
  - When reconciling old freeform plan notes with current Label Studio flows
---

# ExecPlan: Option A — Freeform Spans Golden Set for Recipe Structure (+ Yield/Time), No Tag Annotation

This ExecPlan is a living document. Keep **Progress**, **Surprises & Discoveries**, **Decision Log**, and **Outcomes & Retrospective** up to date as you execute. Maintain this plan in accordance with `docs/PLANS.md`.

## Purpose / Intent (why this matters)

We need a ground-truth dataset to measure whether cookbook ingestion correctly turns messy sources into structured recipes. The highest-leverage human signal is **structure** (titles, ingredient lines, instruction lines, and non-recipe text), because that directly drives downstream parsing, linking, and recipe creation.

Option A deliberately minimizes annotation burden: a small, stable span label set for structure, plus two practical metadata lines (**yield/servings** and **time**) that strongly affect schema alignment. We explicitly avoid asking annotators to label against a large, evolving tag taxonomy (throughput + consistency killer).

Observable “it worked” outcome:

- Label Studio shows a **freeform-spans** project where annotators highlight spans with labels including `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE`.
- `cookimport labelstudio-export --export-scope freeform-spans` produces:
  - `freeform_span_labels.jsonl`
  - `freeform_segment_manifest.jsonl`
  - `summary.json` (and the raw `labelstudio_export.json`)
- `cookimport labelstudio-eval freeform-spans` produces:
  - `eval_report.md`
  - `eval_report.json`
  - `missed_gold_spans.jsonl`
  - `false_positive_preds.jsonl`

## Glossary (terms used here)

- **Source file**: the exact input file bytes (EPUB/PDF/etc.). If bytes change, the source identity changes and eval can collapse to near-zero.
- **Block**: an ordered unit of extracted text with a `block_index` (EPUB paragraph/list item, PDF line/OCR line, etc.).
- **Segment**: a contiguous window of blocks used for freeform annotation, with deterministic ID:
  - `urn:cookimport:segment:{source_hash}:{start_block_index}:{end_block_index}`
- **Gold**: spans labeled by humans in freeform-spans projects, exported as `freeform_span_labels.jsonl`.
- **Predictions (“pred-run”)**: for freeform eval, this is typically the **pipeline** task-scope import run folder (it contains `label_studio_tasks.jsonl` that eval maps into predicted ranges).
- **Write consent**: `--allow-labelstudio-write`. Non-interactive import/benchmark require it; treat as “yes, I intend to upload tasks.”

## Scope (and non-goals)

In scope:

- Freeform spans golden set for structure labels, plus additive `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE`.
- Preserve offset stability (no whitespace normalization changes in freeform rendering).
- Export + eval accept and report new labels without breaking legacy “strict” headline metrics.
- Pilot (3–5 books) → v1 (10–20 books), plus a labeling guide and basic QA/IAA.

Non-goals:

- Manual tagging against the large tag catalog.
- PDF image box annotation workflows (not the current integration).
- Re-architecting benchmark; only guardrails and clarity improvements needed to run safely.

## Progress

- [ ] (2026-02-12) Confirm “Option A” scope + success metrics with stakeholders: freeform spans for structure, plus yield/time lines; **no manual tagging against the 203-tag catalog**.
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Pick a pilot corpus (3–5 cookbooks) that spans: clean EPUB, messy EPUB, and at least one PDF (scanned vs non-scanned if available).
- [ ] (2026-02-12) Run baseline workflow end-to-end on 1 pilot book:
  - freeform import → annotate a few segments → export gold
  - pipeline import (pred-run)
  - freeform eval
  Verify environment, paths, and report artifacts.
- [ ] (2026-02-13) Update freeform Label Studio config to add `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE` (keeping existing labels intact); keep whitespace-preserving rendering unchanged.
- [ ] (2026-02-13) Update export + eval handling so new labels are accepted and reported without breaking legacy exports or existing “strict” headline metrics.
- [ ] (2026-02-14) Write a 1-page labeling guide (with examples) and add it to the repo docs; include “what not to label” rules (e.g., tags, narrative fluff).
- [ ] (2026-02-15) Import pilot tasks with consistent segmentation settings.
- [ ] (2026-02-16) Complete pilot annotations (single annotator) and export gold.
- [ ] (2026-02-17) Run eval; review errors + diagnostics; refine guide + definitions if needed.
- [ ] (2026-02-18) Add second annotator pass for a subset (10–20% of segments) to estimate inter-annotator agreement.
- [ ] (2026-02-20) Expand from pilot to v1 dataset (10–20 cookbooks), cut a release artifact folder, and (optionally) document how this ties into benchmark usage.

## Surprises & Discoveries (keep updated)

- Freeform workflows are segment-based and rely on deterministic IDs for resume/idempotence. This is powerful, but it can surprise you when you want to “re-import the same book” (IAA, reannotation) unless you isolate output dirs.
- Freeform labels intentionally preserve whitespace in the UI to keep offsets stable; any “cleanup” normalization risks breaking span offsets.
- Non-interactive commands default under a golden-root folder and uploads are gated by explicit write-consent flags; accidental upload risk is real if people muscle-memory CLI commands.
- The existing catalog contains a large set of recipe tags; asking annotators to label against that set is a throughput killer and adds consistency risk.

## Decision Log

- **2026-02-12 — Choose Option A (Minimal Human Labeling):** Build a freeform spans golden set focused on structural recipe extraction (title/ingredient/instruction/etc.) and *optionally* yield/time lines; do **not** require humans to label a large tag taxonomy.
- **2026-02-12 — Keep Freeform “Strict Metrics” Stable:** Add yield/time labels as additive diagnostics so headline metrics remain comparable across time; don’t silently redefine the main benchmark.
- **2026-02-12 — Segmentation Defaults:** Start with segment size ~40 blocks and overlap ~5 blocks; adjust only if pilot shows systematic boundary misses.
- **2026-02-12 — Keep freeform gold separate from pipeline preds:** Freeform eval compares gold spans to predictions mapped from pipeline chunks, so treat the “pred-run” as a pipeline import run folder (not the freeform run folder).

## Plan of Work

### Phase 0 — Align on “What we’re measuring”

This is a **structure-first** golden set. Annotators label only spans that correspond to recipe structure (and optionally yield/time lines). Everything else becomes `OTHER`. The dataset is designed to support repeatable benchmarking and to localize failures (ingredients vs narrative, instruction boundary drift, yield/time missed, etc.).

### Phase 1 — Taxonomy + Label Studio config changes (small + additive)

Add two new labels to the existing freeform label config:

- `YIELD_LINE` — spans expressing yield/servings (e.g., “Serves 4”, “Makes 2 loaves”).
- `TIME_LINE` — spans expressing prep/cook/total time (e.g., “Prep: 10 min”, “Total time 1 hour”).

Hard constraints:

- No renaming/removal of existing labels.
- Keep offset stability (preserve whitespace / pre-wrap rendering).
- Do not alter legacy normalization mappings (if older exports exist).

Concrete code touch points to inspect and likely update:

- `cookimport/labelstudio/label_config_freeform.py` (labels + rendering)
- `cookimport/labelstudio/export.py` (freeform export shaping/validation, if any)
- `cookimport/labelstudio/eval_freeform.py` (label normalization + reporting)

Testing expectations:

- Update/add tests in:
  - `tests/test_labelstudio_freeform.py` (config includes new labels; export accepts them)
  - `tests/test_labelstudio_export.py` (fixture with new labels passes)
  - Any eval report/snapshot tests to ensure strict metrics do not change while diagnostics include yield/time counts.

### Phase 2 — Pilot dataset creation (3–5 books)

Goal: validate segmentation, labeling guidance, export/eval reproducibility, and the practical edge cases (messy EPUB + at least one PDF).

Pilot success criteria:

- Imports produce stable task artifacts and reasonable `coverage.json` (no large silent gaps).
- Annotators can label without constantly “what label is this?” questions.
- Exports are generated without patching.
- Eval produces reports and the failure cases are debuggable back to segments.

Segmentation defaults (freeze for pilot):

- `segment_blocks = 40`
- `segment_overlap = 5`

If pilot shows systematic boundary misses (e.g., yield lines often split), adjust once and version the dataset cut. Do not change segmentation mid-campaign without versioning; it changes segment IDs and complicates merges.

### Phase 3 — Evaluation integration (strict metrics stable + yield/time as diagnostics)

Key requirement: keep existing headline/strict metrics comparable over time. The safest pattern:

- Include `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE` in exports.
- In freeform eval reporting, treat yield/time as **additive diagnostics** (counts + per-label metrics), not part of the strict aggregate unless you explicitly version/change the headline metric definition.

### Phase 4 — Scale to v1 (10–20 books) + QA + IAA

Scale annotation with:

- A clear labeling guide.
- Periodic spot checks (20 segments/book).
- A 10–20% overlap subset labeled by a second annotator to estimate agreement and highlight ambiguity.

Produce a versioned dataset bundle folder with:

- corpus list (files + hashes),
- segmentation params,
- label set version,
- date range + annotators,
- known caveats (OCR-heavy PDFs, etc.),
- per-book eval reports.

## Risks and Mitigations (plus footguns)

### Offset drift / unstable spans
Mitigation: preserve whitespace in rendered text; prohibit normalization; add a smoke test that offsets still align to exported segment text.

### Accidental uploads / write-side effects
Mitigation: keep write-consent explicit; document “no write without intent”; keep pilot/v1 projects clearly named.

### Benchmark side effects + gold discovery footgun
Non-interactive benchmark always uploads predictions first; it is not “eval-only.” Also, gold discovery searches both `data/golden/**` and `data/output/**`. If multiple gold exports exist, it can select the wrong one.
Mitigation: run benchmark in a clean workspace (or use explicit paths via `labelstudio-eval`); avoid mixing unrelated exports in the same roots during a campaign.

### Source identity mismatches leading to “zero match” eval
Mitigation: keep the exact source bytes stable; avoid renames/cutdown variants during labeling. Do not default to `--force-source-match`; use it only when you knowingly compare variants and accept the risk of masking mismatches.

### Segmentation too small/large
Mitigation: tune after pilot; version if changed; do not change mid-run.

### Label ambiguity (NOTES vs TIP vs OTHER; yield/time boundaries)
Mitigation: crisp definitions + examples; add an “if unsure, label OTHER unless clearly TIP/NOTES” rule; adjudicate repeated disagreements.

## Definition of Done

- Freeform label config includes `YIELD_LINE` and `TIME_LINE` and preserves existing labels + offset-stable rendering.
- Exported gold includes:
  - `freeform_span_labels.jsonl`
  - `freeform_segment_manifest.jsonl`
  - `summary.json` (and raw export)
- Freeform eval runs cleanly on pilot and v1 datasets and produces:
  - `eval_report.json`
  - `eval_report.md`
  - `missed_gold_spans.jsonl`
  - `false_positive_preds.jsonl`
- A concise labeling guide exists with:
  - label definitions + boundary rules,
  - “what not to label” section,
  - yield/time edge cases,
  - versioned segmentation settings.
- v1 dataset bundle (10–20 books) is reproducible from documented commands and ready to be used as a benchmarking input.

## Labels (Freeform-Spans)

Base labels (existing):

- `RECIPE_TITLE`
- `INGREDIENT_LINE`
- `INSTRUCTION_LINE`
- `TIP`
- `NOTES`
- `VARIANT`
- `OTHER`

Additive labels (Option A extension):

- `YIELD_LINE`
- `TIME_LINE`

High-level labeling rules:

- Label the smallest span that cleanly expresses the target.
- Prefer line-level spans for ingredients/instructions/yield/time.
- If unsure whether something is “real recipe content” vs prose, label `OTHER` unless it clearly fits `TIP` or `NOTES`.

## Recommended CLI Runbook (Non-Interactive)

Prereqs:

- Label Studio running + env vars set:
  - `LABEL_STUDIO_URL`
  - `LABEL_STUDIO_API_KEY`

Notes on output roots:

- Label Studio CLI defaults its artifacts under `data/golden/` (not `data/output/`).
- Non-interactive upload/write is gated by `--allow-labelstudio-write`.

### 1) Import (freeform spans) — gold project

Use consistent segmentation settings for the entire campaign:

    cookimport labelstudio-import data/input/<book>.epub \
      --task-scope freeform-spans \
      --segment-blocks 40 \
      --segment-overlap 5 \
      --allow-labelstudio-write

Annotate in Label Studio.

### 2) Export gold

    cookimport labelstudio-export \
      --project-name "<Freeform Project Name>" \
      --export-scope freeform-spans

Record the resulting path to:

- `<gold_spans_jsonl>` = `.../exports/freeform_span_labels.jsonl`

### 3) Import (pipeline) — prediction run (“pred-run”)

Freeform eval expects predicted labeled ranges mapped from pipeline chunks, so generate a pipeline run folder:

    cookimport labelstudio-import data/input/<book>.epub \
      --task-scope pipeline \
      --chunk-level both \
      --allow-labelstudio-write

Record `<pred_run_dir>` = the run folder created for this pipeline import (it contains `label_studio_tasks.jsonl`).

### 4) Eval (freeform spans)

Default: do NOT force-match unless you explicitly accept comparing variants.

    cookimport labelstudio-eval freeform-spans \
      --pred-run <pred_run_dir> \
      --gold-spans <gold_spans_jsonl> \
      --output-dir data/golden/<ts>/eval-freeform/<book_slug>/

If (and only if) you intentionally compare renamed/cutdown variants, you may add `--force-source-match`, but document why.

### 5) Benchmark (convenience, but upload-first)

    cookimport labelstudio-benchmark \
      --allow-labelstudio-write

Warning: benchmark is upload-first; it will import/upload predictions before scoring. Also, gold discovery searches both `data/golden/**` and `data/output/**`; clean your workspace or use explicit `labelstudio-eval` paths for safety.

## Dataset Versioning

For every dataset cut, record:

- corpus list (books + versions/hashes),
- segmentation params (`segment_blocks`, `segment_overlap`),
- label set version (including yield/time enabled),
- date range + annotators,
- known caveats (OCR-heavy PDFs, etc.).

## Practical Quality Checks

- Randomly sample 20 segments per book:
  - confirm RECIPE_TITLE vs section headers are consistent,
  - confirm ingredients aren’t being confused with instruction steps,
  - confirm yield/time are consistently captured when present.
- After export, spot-check:
  - span offsets still align to displayed text,
  - touched block indices look plausible (no wildly out-of-range indices).

## Outcomes & Retrospective

(To be completed after v1 dataset ships.)

- What changed in extraction quality?
- Where did label ambiguity remain?
- What should be automated next?
```

## docs/tasks/2026-02-15_22.27.19 - interactive-export-project-before-scope.md

```markdown
---
summary: "Reorder interactive Label Studio export prompts so project selection happens before export scope."
read_when:
  - "When changing interactive Label Studio export menu order"
---

# Problem statement

Interactive Label Studio export asks for `export_scope` before project name selection. This is backwards for normal user intent and causes unnecessary cognitive load.

# Acceptance criteria

- Interactive `labelstudio_export` asks project selection before `Export scope`.
- Existing scope values (`pipeline`, `canonical-blocks`, `freeform-spans`) still route to `run_labelstudio_export(...)` unchanged.
- Docs reflect the new order.

# Verification steps

- Fail-before: `. .venv/bin/activate && pytest -q tests/test_labelstudio_benchmark_helpers.py -k interactive_labelstudio_export_selects_project_before_scope`
- Pass-after: `. .venv/bin/activate && pytest -q tests/test_labelstudio_benchmark_helpers.py -k "interactive_labelstudio_export_selects_project_before_scope or interactive_labelstudio_export_routes_to_export_command or select_export_project_name"`

# Evidence

- Fail-before: new order test fails because `Export scope` appeared before project selection.
- Pass-after: targeted export-order and export-routing tests pass.

# Constraints/gotchas

- Keep credential resolution order unchanged.
- Keep manual-entry fallback behavior for project selection unchanged.

# Decision

Reordered only the interactive export prompts in `cookimport/cli.py` and added a focused regression test for prompt order. This is the smallest behavioral change that matches expected UX.

# Rollback / compensation plan

Revert prompt order in `cookimport/cli.py` and remove the new order regression test.
```

## docs/tasks/2026-02-15_22.59.30 - split-merge-visibility-and-topic-hash-cache.md

```markdown
---
summary: "Make split-merge progress visible and remove repeated source hashing during topic-candidate writes."
read_when:
  - "When merge appears stuck after worker jobs complete"
  - "When tuning stage write-time performance for knowledge-heavy EPUB/PDF runs"
---

# Problem statement

Split runs could look hung after worker completion because `MainProcess` stayed on a generic merge label while doing long write work. Knowledge-heavy runs also spent excessive merge write time repeatedly hashing the same source file while assigning topic IDs.

# Acceptance criteria

- Main-process split merge emits phase-level status updates in the worker dashboard.
- Topic-candidate output writing hashes the source file once per file version (not once per candidate).
- Regression tests cover both behaviors.

# Verification steps

- Fail-before (on pre-change baseline):
  - `. .venv/bin/activate && pytest -q tests/test_tip_writer.py::test_write_topic_candidates_hashes_source_file_once tests/test_split_merge_status.py::test_merge_split_jobs_reports_main_process_phases`
- Pass-after:
  - `. .venv/bin/activate && pytest -q tests/test_tip_writer.py tests/test_split_merge_status.py`

# Evidence

- Pass-after command succeeds (`3 passed`).
- New merge status test verifies callback phases include topic-candidate writing/report/raw-merge steps.
- New writer test verifies only one `_hash_file` call while writing multiple topic candidates.

# Constraints/gotchas

- Keep split merge output contract unchanged (same files and IDs).
- Progress updates must be best-effort and never fail merge execution.

# Decision

Add a status callback path to split merge helpers and metadata-based hash caching in writer hash resolution.

# Rollback / compensation plan

- Remove status callback plumbing from split-merge helpers and revert to static merge labels.
- Remove cached hash helper and return to direct `_hash_file` calls in `_resolve_file_hash`.
```

## docs/tasks/2026-02-15_23.14.04 - interactive-benchmark-credential-prompt.md

```markdown
# Decision
```

## docs/understandings/2026-02-15_22.27.19-interactive-export-prompt-order.md

```markdown

summary: "Interactive Label Studio export currently asked for scope before project due to prompt order in cli.py."

  - "When changing interactive Label Studio export prompts or back-navigation behavior"
---

# Interactive export prompt order (2026-02-15)

Discovery:
- In `cookimport/cli.py`, interactive `labelstudio_export` asked `Export scope` before `_select_export_project_name(...)`.
- This is why users had to pick category/type before project title.
```

## docs/understandings/2026-02-15_22.34.31-export-project-type-detection.md

```markdown
---
summary: "Export picker type labels are derived from local manifests first, then Label Studio payload heuristics."
read_when:
  - "When a project in interactive export shows type: unknown"
---

# Export picker type detection (2026-02-15)

Discovery:
- `LabelStudioClient.list_projects()` does not reliably provide a direct task scope field.
- The project title list alone cannot show category/type without extra lookup.

Decision:
- Primary source: most recent local `manifest.json` per project (`task_scope`).
- Fallback: infer scope from `label_config` tokens in the Label Studio project payload.
- Final fallback: display `unknown` when no reliable signal exists.
```

## docs/understandings/2026-02-15_22.48.59-report-metadata-flow.md

```markdown
---
summary: "How stage report metadata is populated across single-file and split-job EPUB/PDF paths."
read_when:
  - "When adding fields to *.excel_import_report.json"
  - "When debugging missing report keys in split-job runs"
---

# Report metadata flow

Discovery:
- Single-file runs write reports in `cli_worker.stage_one_file`.
- Split EPUB/PDF runs write a fresh merged report in `cli._merge_split_jobs`.

Implication:
- Fields set only inside importer-level reports can be lost in split runs unless also written in merge-path report construction.

Current rule:
- `importerName` and `runConfig` are now set in both single-file and split-merge report paths so report metadata is consistent.
```
